guid: GUID-66CBF3AE-39E8-4412-AF3E-1A6D56951B73
title: " grclear (AutoLISP)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-66CBF3AE-39E8-4412-AF3E-1A6D56951B73.htm
---



---
---
guid: GUID-67150A48-FF70-4CC7-8C6E-21DEF6838C82
title: "To Create a Hatch Pattern with Dashed Lines "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-B67FADB9-0F10-4536-ABC4-BB7D8BDDF5B1
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-67150A48-FF70-4CC7-8C6E-21DEF6838C82.htm
---

1. Open an existing PAT file or create a new file in a text editor that saves in ASCII format (for example, Notepad on Windows or TextEdit on Mac OS).
2. Create a header line that includes an asterisk and a pattern name. The name of the hatch pattern is limited to 31 characters.
3. (Optional) Include a description in the header line, follow the pattern name with a comma and description text.
4. Create a descriptor line that includes
   * An angle at which the line is drawn
   * An origin point
   * A of any value if you want to offset alternating lines in the line family
   * A of any value
   * A value for a dash length
   * A value for a dot length
   * An optional second value for a different dash length
   * An optional second value for a different dot length
5. Add a blank line after the last descriptor line.

---

guid: GUID-6C42C6DA-51BD-42D7-8532-933A38F1CAA4
title: "To Compile a Single AutoLISP Program File (Visual LISP IDE)"

parent_guid: GUID-13E30BCF-CF1F-4124-B694-C5B523258411

---

* At the AutoCAD Command prompt, use the function using the following syntax:

  ```
  (vlisp-compile ' “” [])
  ```

  + is a symbol identifying the compiler mode
  + is a string naming the source file
  + is a string naming the compiled output file

   .

guid: GUID-6C90EFB8-AACF-4160-8E22-861DB3CF02C9
title: "About Migrating and Transferring Custom Settings"
depth: 2
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-6C90EFB8-AACF-4160-8E22-861DB3CF02C9.htm

---
---
guid: GUID-6CAA2BEE-6CDF-44B7-B921-272B1565031B
title: "To Configure a Data Source Using OLE DB"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-1C006BB3-9909-420B-B5D7-791E2B104C46
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-6CAA2BEE-6CDF-44B7-B921-272B1565031B.htm
---

1. Use Microsoft ODBC to set up a data source.
2. At the Command prompt, enter .
3. On the dbConnect Manager, right-click Data Sources and click Configure Data Source.
4. In the Configure a Data Source dialog box, do one of the following:
   * In the Data Source Name box, enter a name for the data source. Click OK.
   * In the Data Sources list box, select a data source. Click OK.
5. In the Data Link Properties dialog box, Provider tab, select Microsoft OLE DB Provider for ODBC Drivers. Click Next.
6. In the Use Data Source Name box, enter the name of the data source you want to configure.
7. Click Test Connection to verify that your configuration is working properly.
8. Click OK.

---
guid: GUID-75F19C76-78D0-443B-BC39-EB9FEB4650B1
title: "About Using AutoCAD Commands (AutoLISP)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-8A0FE094-4547-4767-BE8A-5C10B248CF02
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-75F19C76-78D0-443B-BC39-EB9FEB4650B1.htm
---

```
(defun c:CircC ()
  (command "._circle" "0,0" "3,3")
  (command "._thickness" 1)
  (command "._circle" PAUSE PAUSE)
 (princ)
)
```

1. The first call to
   passes points to the CIRCLE command as strings (draws a circle centered at 0.0,0.0 and passes through 3.0,3.0).
2. The second call to command passes an integer to the THICKNESS system variable (changes the current thickness to 1.0).
3. The last call to command prompts the user for a center point and then the radius of the circle.

```
(defun c:CircCS ( / p1 rad)
  (command-s "._circle" "0,0" "3,3")
  (command-s "._thickness" 1)
  (setq p1 (getpoint "\nEnter a center point: "))
  (setq rad (getdist p1 "\nEnter a radius: "))
  (command-s "._circle" p1 rad)
 (princ)
)
```

---
guid: GUID-772665E3-DD69-4785-A7DD-0B256B7B22F2
title: "Selecting Text in the Text Editor Reference (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-CAD3B7DA-0295-4ABE-91A4-AA7617BA263C
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-772665E3-DD69-4785-A7DD-0B256B7B22F2.htm
---

* If the cursor immediately precedes an open parenthesis or double quotation mark, the following text up to the matching close parenthesis or double quotation mark is selected.
* If the cursor immediately follows a close parenthesis or double quotation mark, all preceding text up to the matching open parenthesis or double quotation mark is selected.
* If the cursor immediately precedes or follows a word, or is within a word, only that word is selected.

  is not installed with the AutoCAD program. To obtain this documentation, download the ObjectARX SDK (Software Development Kit) from the
  . The
  is available from the AutoCAD product help. (Managed .NET development is not supported in AutoCAD LT for Windows, and on Mac OS and Web)

guid: GUID-7AA47EDC-DC21-4063-9DA2-33632A4115DD
title: "To Perform a Long-Axis Plot (HP-GL/2 Device)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-93357112-AC38-4E1F-B35C-79369388BA1D
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-7AA47EDC-DC21-4063-9DA2-33632A4115DD.htm
---

1. Plot a drawing using a device that has been configured with the HP-GL/2 driver.
2. To stop your plotter after the program has finished sending all the vectors, clear the plotter memory using the plotter's Control Panel.
3. To stop a long-axis plot while the program is sending vectors to the plotter, press Esc.
4. Clear the plotter memory as indicated for the following devices:
   * Press the Cancel button.
   * Press the plotter Reset button.
   * Press the Plot Management button. Select Queuing Operations, and then select the plot and delete it from the queue.
   * Press the Cancel button.
   * Press the Cancel button.

guid: GUID-7ACCD6D8-BCB2-477C-AB38-977A935F7C4D
title: "FAQ: How Can I Improve the Performance of an AutoCAD-based Product?"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-1436634D-B2EA-4B77-A1F9-577042E3EA3A
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-7ACCD6D8-BCB2-477C-AB38-977A935F7C4D.htm
---

* Make sure your hardware exceeds the minimum system requirements for the AutoCAD-based product. For information on new systems that have been certified for the latest release, see
  . While certified hardware does not guarantee a particular system will meet your particular needs, it does reflect that the hardware supports the advanced features in the latest release.
* Use a certified graphics card driver for the AutoCAD-based product.
* Install the latest Service Pack for the AutoCAD-based product.
* Enable hardware acceleration for use in the AutoCAD-based product:
  1. On the status bar, right-click the Hardware Acceleration button ( )Graphics Performance.
  2. In the Graphics Performance dialog box, turn on Hardware Acceleration.
* Install the latest service pack and updates for your operating system.
* Optimize your operating system by enabling available performance features and disabling those that affect graphical performance that you do not need. For more information on improving the performance of your operating system, see the documentation that was provided with your operating system

guid: GUID-7BA45202-D95F-4F2D-8D83-965024826074
title: " cond (AutoLISP)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-7BA45202-D95F-4F2D-8D83-965024826074.htm

---
---
guid: GUID-7BE00235-5D40-4789-9E34-D57685E83875
title: "Getting Started with Visual Studio Code "
depth: 3
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-7BE00235-5D40-4789-9E34-D57685E83875.htm
---

1. - VS Code isn't part of the AutoCAD install, and must be downloaded and installed separately. The version of VS Code built by Microsoft can be downloaded from the
   . See
   for a general overview on how to download and install VS Code.
2. - While VS Code can be used to edit AutoLISP source (LSP) files without doing anything additional, it won't understand the syntax of or how to debug an AutoLISP program without installing the AutoCAD AutoLISP Extension. The AutoCAD AutoLISP Extension contains a set of special functions that provide syntax checking in the editor window and the ability to attach VS Code to AutoCAD which allows you to load and debug your custom programs. See
   for steps on how to locate and install the AutoCAD AutoLISP Extension from the VS Code Extensions Marketplace.
3. - Debug configurations are used to inform VS Code as to which application should be used when testing and debugging your custom AutoLISP programs. There are two different debug configurations available for use with the AutoCAD AutoLISP Extension; AutoCAD Debug Attach and AutoCAD Debug Launch. These debug configurations are stored as part of the extension's settings. See
   for information on how to setup these debug configurations.
4. - AutoLISP projects allow you to logically group AutoLISP source (LSP) files. An AutoLISP project is saved to a file with the
   extension. After an AutoLISP project has been opened in the AutoLISP Project Manager, you can add, edit, and remove LSP files. For information on using the AutoLISP Project Manager, see
   and
   .
5. - LSP files opened in VS Code with the AutoCAD AutoLISP Extension installed are evaluated for proper syntax and can be edited using extension specific features; autocomplete, code snippets, code formatting, and many more. For information on how to create, open, and edit LSP files in VS Code, see
   ,
   , and
   .
6. - After adding the AutoLISP debug configurations to VS Code and opening an LSP file, you can step through and debug the AutoLISP statements stored in the LSP file. VS Code provides a variety of tools that allow you to watch the values of variables, set breakpoints and step through statements, inspect the current call stack, and much more. See
   for information on how to debug AutoLISP programs with VS Code and the AutoCAD AutoLISP Extension.
7. - Optionally, before deploying your custom programs, you can compile your LSP files to protect the original source code. Based on the method used to compile an LSP file, either a FAS or VLX file is built. For information on how to compile your LSP files, see
   .
8. - Once you have tested and debugged your AutoLISP programs, they are ready for deployment. Deploying your AutoLISP programs can be as simple as copying them to a local or network drive, bundling them into a plug-in, or installing them with an installation program. Copying the files directly to a drive is often the simplest approach, but you will also need to setup AutoCAD to locate and load your programs. See
   and
   for information on loading and creating plug-in bundles for your AutoLISP programs.

---

guid: GUID-7D90B23D-CC35-4D05-A62D-330AFF39F678
title: "To Create a Plotter Configuration for the System Printer "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-14CCDF22-075C-4668-A4D2-F310DBDB35DE
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-7D90B23D-CC35-4D05-A62D-330AFF39F678.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the Add-a-Plotter Wizard shortcut icon.
3. On the Begin page, select System Printer. Click Next.
4. On the System Printer page, select the system printer for which you want to create a plotter configuration file. Click Next.
5. On the Import PCP or PC2 page, click Next to continue.
6. On the Plotter Name page, enter a name for the plotter configuration file. Click Next.
7. On the Finish page, click Finish.

title: " acdimenableupdate (AutoLISP)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-7E10D18A-6FD6-4B20-A981-27FF77C2F042.htm

---
---
guid: GUID-7E1BFC62-C5F2-48C6-84D7-71FAD4DF0BEF
title: "To Create a Simple Hatch Pattern "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-A6F2E6FF-1717-44B6-A476-0CA817ADD77E
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-7E1BFC62-C5F2-48C6-84D7-71FAD4DF0BEF.htm
---

1. Open an existing PAT file or create a new file in a text editor that saves in ASCII format (for example, Notepad on Windows or TextEdit on Mac OS).
2. Create a header line that begins with an asterisk and includes a pattern name that is no more than 31 characters in length.
3. Optionally, include a description for the hatch pattern by adding a comma and descriptive text after the pattern name.
4. Create a descriptor line that includes
   * An angle at which the line is drawn
   * An
     origin point
   * A
     of 0
   * A
     of any value
5. Add a blank line after the descriptor line.

depth: 4
parent_guid: nan

---
---
guid: GUID-7F024C1B-EFB8-4F6C-9EFE-A6491210A4CD
title: "About Accessing and Requesting User Input (AutoLISP)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-53B1A2A4-3E63-4699-BFDC-C67A04492469
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-7F024C1B-EFB8-4F6C-9EFE-A6491210A4CD.htm
---

* – Reads values from any of the AutoCAD input devices.
* – Establishes keywords and controls certain types of input for use by the next user-input function call.
* – Pauses for the input of a string and returns that string.
* – Pauses for the input of a point and returns that point.
* – Pauses for the input of an integer and returns that integer.
* – Pauses for the input of a distance and returns a real number.
* – Pauses for the input of an angle and returns the angle expressed in radians.

---
guid: GUID-8028B340-AA7B-4DD1-832F-8270755DBA7D
title: "To Adjust Port Settings"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-DD9C98E9-BC4A-4E54-837A-53CF80222A1B
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-8028B340-AA7B-4DD1-832F-8270755DBA7D.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the plotter configuration (PC3) file whose port settings you want to change.
3. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, click the Ports tab.
4. Select one of the following options:
   * Sends the drawing to the printer through the specified port.
   * Sends the drawing to the file name specified on the Files tab in the Options dialog box.
   * Uses the AutoSpool utility specified on the Files tab in the Options dialog box to plot the drawing.
5. For a device that emulates the configured device and has additional port options, select Show All Ports.
6. To connect a nonsystem plotter to another instance of the device, click Browse Network. In the Browse for Printer dialog box, select the device and click OK.
7. Click OK.

---
---
guid: GUID-802F0B23-62E3-4341-AF40-6D899B221298
title: "To Start Debugging a Program (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-5424079C-26CD-4E7D-819A-DE7B7B340077
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-802F0B23-62E3-4341-AF40-6D899B221298.htm
---

1. In Visual LISP, click Debug Stop Once.
2. Open the program you want to execute and debug.
3. Click Tools Load Text in Editor.
4. At the AutoCAD command prompt, enter the command or function to begin the execution of the program.
5. Click Debug Step Into, Step Over, or Step Out to step through the code expressions that define the command or function.
6. Click Debug Continue to exit the break loop and resume normal execution of the program.

title: " vl-exit-with-value (AutoLISP)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-80622A39-A5E8-4E68-824E-E66BD8D3E9DE.htm

---
---
guid: GUID-80F488C9-3CBA-428F-8C80-85B3D1564C25
title: "Stack Element List Reference (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-71751025-1ECA-44C5-B7CF-71B728B89AAD
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-80F488C9-3CBA-428F-8C80-85B3D1564C25.htm
---

* Function call frames show one individual function invocation. They are displayed in the following format:

  ```
   ( {} )
  ```
* Keyword frames are displayed at the very top and bottom of a trace stack. They are displayed in the following format:

  ```
   : - {}
  ```
* Top forms indicate an action that was initiated by typing an expression at the top-level Console window, or from the invocation of a function that was triggered during the loading of a file or selection within a Visual LISP text editor window.
* Lambda forms are placed within a stack whenever a function is encountered within a program.
* Special forms display the invocation of the and functions. The arguments for these functions are not displayed. They are displayed in the following format:

  ```
   ( )
  ```

```
(defun stack-tracing (indexVal maxVal)
   (princ "At the top of the stack-tracing function, indexVal = ")
   (princ indexVal)
   (if (< indexVal maxVal)
      (stack-tracing (1+ indexVal) maxVal)
      (princ "Reached the maximum depth.") ; place a breakpoint
                                          ; at the beginning of
                                          ; this line
   )
)

(defun c:trace-10-deep ()
   (terpri)
   (stack-tracing 1 10)
)
```

guid: GUID-877B87BA-6FA2-4894-9F94-184E7DF25B7D
title: "About Dotted Pairs (AutoLISP)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-F0E08704-2854-4E05-9096-3A3ACEA007EB
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-877B87BA-6FA2-4894-9F94-184E7DF25B7D.htm
---

```

(LYR . "WALLS")
```

* - Returns the first member of the specified dotted pair.
* - Returns the second member of the specified dotted pair.
* - Searches an association list for a member and returns that association list entry.
* - Returns the nth element of a list.

```

((LYR . "WALLS") (LEN . 240.0) (HGT . 96.0))
```

```

(LEN . 240.0)

"WALLS"

(LEN . 240.0)

LEN
```

---
guid: GUID-877CEEA5-0D88-48DF-8450-B9421031A1B7
title: "About Relational Tests in Filter Lists for Selection Sets (AutoLISP)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-7BE77062-C359-4D01-915B-69CF672C653B
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-877CEEA5-0D88-48DF-8450-B9421031A1B7.htm
---

```
(ssget "X" '((0 . "CIRCLE") (-4 . ">=") (40 . 2.0)))
```

* All relational operators except for the bitwise operators ( and
  ) are valid for both real- and integer-valued groups.
* The bitwise operators
  and
  are valid only for integer-valued groups.
* For point group codes, the
  ,
  , and
  tests can be combined into a single string, with each operator separated by commas (for example,). If an operator is omitted from the string (for example,
  leaves out the
  test), then the “anything goes” operator,
  , is assumed.
* Direction vectors (group code 210) can be compared only with the operators
  ,
  , and
  (or one of the equivalent “not equal” strings).
* You cannot use the relational operators with string group codes; use wild-card tests instead.

guid: GUID-88B8FCE4-17A5-4799-AB85-B14C8DB602D5
title: "To Test the Use of Private Data from a VLX File (AutoLISP/Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-2B4C9290-CFE3-4430-B543-61ED38A7C170
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-88B8FCE4-17A5-4799-AB85-B14C8DB602D5.htm
---

1. Enter the following commands at the Visual LISP Console window:

   ```

   "Mumbo Dumbo"

   "Mumbo Dumbo"
   ```
2. Enter the following code in a file and use Make Application to build a VLX from the file. Use the Expert mode of the Make Application wizard, and select the Separate Namespace option on the Compile Options tab.

   ```
   (vl-doc-export 'ldataput)
   (vl-doc-export 'ldataget)
   (vl-doc-export 'ldataget-nilt)

   (defun ldataput ()
     (princ "This is a test of putting private ldata ")
     (vlax-ldata-put "mydict" "mykey" "Mine! Mine! " T)
   )

   (defun ldataget ()
     (vlax-ldata-get "mydict" "mykey")
   )

   (defun ldataget-nilt ()
     (vlax-ldata-get "mydict" "mykey" nil T)
   )
   ```
3. Load the VLX file.
4. Run
   to save private data:

   ```

   This is a test of putting private ldata
   ```
5. Run
   to retrieve LISP data:

   ```

   "Mumbo Dumbo"
   ```

   ```

   "Mine! Mine!"
   ```
6. Run
   to retrieve LISP data:

   ```

   "Mine! Mine!"
   ```
7. From the Console prompt, issue the same call that
   uses to retrieve private data:

   ```

   "Mumbo Dumbo"
   ```

guid: GUID-8A1D3D8B-54C6-4693-ACF8-2B317EC11193
title: "acet-reg-user-prodkey (AutoLISP/Express Tools)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-8A1D3D8B-54C6-4693-ACF8-2B317EC11193.htm

---
guid: GUID-8A218F37-5660-47D2-B6C4-FDB2C9E631AF
title: "To Set Up a Microsoft Excel Data Source Using ODBC"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-1C006BB3-9909-420B-B5D7-791E2B104C46
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-8A218F37-5660-47D2-B6C4-FDB2C9E631AF.htm
---

1. Click the Windows Start button Windows System Control Panel.
2. Double-click the Administrative Tools icon, and then double-click Data Sources (ODBC).
3. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, do one of the following:
   * Click the User DSN tab to create a data source that is visible only to you and can be used only on the computer you create it in.
   * Click the System DSN tab to create a data source that is visible to all users who have access rights to the computer.
   * Click the File DSN tab to create a data source that can be shared with other users who have the same ODBC drivers installed on their systems.
4. Click Add.
5. Select the Microsoft Excel Driver, and then click Finish.
6. Enter a name for your data source in Data Source Name, and select the appropriate version of Excel from the Version list.
7. Make sure that Use Current Directory is cleared.
8. Click Select Workbook, and then locate and select the workbook or spreadsheet you want to configure. Click OK.
9. In the ODBC Microsoft Excel dialog box, click OK.
10. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, click OK.

---

---
guid: GUID-8A8B35C8-AE0C-4C32-A063-FBF718390C0D
title: "Understanding the Gp:recalcPolyCorners Function"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-209318DE-95C4-40F6-8776-935C8905FDEE
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Tutorials/files/GUID-8A8B35C8-AE0C-4C32-A063-FBF718390C0D.htm
---



---
---
guid: GUID-8A8F6924-9B1C-41E6-A0E9-3A95DD96CD42
title: "To Create a Simple Linetype From the Command Prompt"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-EF1DF0A9-2088-487C-8085-16FEE6425405
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-8A8F6924-9B1C-41E6-A0E9-3A95DD96CD42.htm
---

1. At the Command prompt, enter .
2. Enter and press Enter.
3. Enter a name for the linetype and press Enter.
4. In the Create or Append Linetype File dialog box, select an existing LIN linetype file or enter a new file name in the File Name box. Click Save.
5. (Optional) Enter text that describes the new linetype and press Enter.
6. At the Enter Linetype Pattern prompt, specify the pattern for the tinetype and press Enter. Follow these guidelines:
   * All linetypes must begin with a dash.
   * Enter zeros for dots.
   * Enter negative real numbers for spaces. The value defines the length of the space in drawing units.
   * Enter positive real numbers for dashes. The value defines the length of the dash in drawing units.
   * Separate each dot, dash, or space value from the next with a comma.
   * Use a space between a dot and a dash.
7. Press Enter to end the command.

url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-8ADB32CB-8181-4126-BDB3-7D7738AB819A.htm
---



---
---
guid: GUID-8AE6163C-BBB0-4862-96F1-EB49923E317D
title: "About Creating Shortcut Menus"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-8AE6163C-BBB0-4862-96F1-EB49923E317D.htm
---

* - Displayed when you right-click in the drawing area while a grip on an object is selected.
* - Displayed when you hold Shift and right-click in the drawing area.
* - Displayed when you right-click in the drawing area while no command is active and no objects are selected.
* - Displayed when you right-click in the drawing area while a command is active. In addition to the content of the menu, the command’s options (keywords within the square brackets) are inserted into this menu.
* - Displayed when you right-click in the drawing area while one or more objects are selected, no grips are selected, and no command is active.

(setq index ( get_tile "justone"))
(cond
  ((/= index "")                   ;See if string is empty.
    (= 2 (atoi index))
    .                              ; Process the third entry.
    .
    .
  )
)
```

```
(defun MK_LIST (readlist / count item retlist)
  (setq count 1)
  (while (setq item (read readlist))
    (setq retlist (cons (nth item displist) retlist))
    (while (and (/= " " (substr readlist count 1))
                       (/= "" (substr readlist count 1)))
      (setq count (1+ count))
    )
    (setq readlist (substr readlist count))
  )
  (reverse retlist)
)
```

---
guid: GUID-8FBE6A29-EE60-4134-920A-091D747718EA
title: "To Use AutoSpool"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-CD9B5B2F-74A0-4C69-9176-A8BE717B833F
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-8FBE6A29-EE60-4134-920A-091D747718EA.htm
---

1. In
   , click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the plotter configuration (PC3) file whose port settings you want to change.
3. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, Ports tab, select AutoSpool.
4. Click OK.
5. In
   , click Application menu Options.
6. In the Options dialog box, Files tab, click the plus sign (+) next to Print file, Spooler, and Prolog Section Names to expand the node.
7. Click the plus sign (+) next to Print Spool Executable to expand it.
8. Select the item and click Browse.
9. In the Select a File dialog box, locate the program you want to execute when the plot file has been created. Click Open.
10. Add any command line arguments you want to use.
11. Click Apply.

guid: GUID-8FCBEB50-38D7-4A1C-A88D-A4ACA2B23292
title: "acet-file-attr (AutoLISP/Express Tools)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-8FCBEB50-38D7-4A1C-A88D-A4ACA2B23292.htm

---
---
guid: GUID-8FD70C14-B534-4E2A-BD80-75C0E7416E5D
title: "To Configure a Local, Nonsystem Plotter"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-D1786BA2-1CB1-4585-AA6A-6ED8088D4B28
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-8FD70C14-B534-4E2A-BD80-75C0E7416E5D.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. In the Autodesk Plotter Manager, double-click the Add-a-Plotter Wizard shortcut.
3. In the Add-a-Plotter wizard, read the Introduction, and then click Next to advance to the Add Plotter - Begin page.
4. On the Add Plotter - Begin page, click My Computer. Click Next.
5. On the Add Plotter - Plotter Model page, select a manufacturer and model. Click Next.
6. On the Import PCP or PC2 page, click Next to continue.
7. On the Add Plotter - Ports page, select the port to use when plotting. Click Next. The ports available for the specified device are displayed.
8. On the Add Plotter - Plotter Name page, enter a name to identify the currently configured plotter. Click Next.
9. When you reach the Add Plotter - Finish page, you can click Finish to exit the Add-a-Plotter wizard.

guid: GUID-907A8502-BFFF-4AA3-B340-6A490676BF7C
title: "To Set the Timeout Value for Network or Windows System Printers "
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-3E9066ED-9430-4EEA-9DBA-6156AAA0D5A5

6. Click OK.

---
guid: GUID-91ACA03D-4C4A-4275-B8BC-A123EA374111
title: "To Set Up a Direct Microsoft Access Configuration Using OLE DB"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-1C006BB3-9909-420B-B5D7-791E2B104C46
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-91ACA03D-4C4A-4275-B8BC-A123EA374111.htm
---

1. At the Command prompt, enter .
2. On the dbConnect Manager, right-click Data Sources and click Configure Data Source.
3. In the Configure a Data Source dialog box, do one of the following:
   * In the Data Source Name box, enter a name for the data source. Click OK.
   * In the Data Sources list box, select a data source. Click OK.
4. In the Data Link Properties dialog box, Provider tab, select Microsoft Jet 4.0 OLE DB Provider. Click Next.
5. In the Database Name box, enter the name and path to the database you want to configure.
6. Click Test Connection to verify that your configuration is working properly.
7. Click OK.

---
---
guid: GUID-92DA21E0-1E33-45AD-B2F8-1AB788392E4B
title: "About Controlling Menus (AutoLISP)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-A7AEB9D4-1E5E-49D2-832A-7AFCE51C10BE
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-92DA21E0-1E33-45AD-B2F8-1AB788392E4B.htm
---

```
(menucmd )
```

```
(menucmd "P0=POP0") ; Loads the POP0 menu into the P0 menu area
(menucmd "P0=*")    ; Display it
```

```
(menucmd "P1=*")
```

```
(menucmd "P1=MORESTUFF") ; Loads the MORESTUFF menu in the P1 menu location
(menucmd "P1=*")         ; Displays it
```

```
(menucmd "P1=POP1")
```

```
(menucmd "P2.4=#?") ; If disabled returns "P2.4=~"
```

```
(menucmd "P2.4=")  ; Enables the label
(menucmd "P2.4=~") ; Disables the label
```

```
(menucmd "Gacad.ID_New=~") ; Disables the label
(menucmd "Gacad.ID_New=")  ; Enables the label
```

```
(defun C:CTIME ( / ctim)
  (setq ctim
  (menucmd "M=$(edtime,$(getvar,date),H:MMam/pm)"))
  (princ (strcat "\nThe current time is " ctim ))
 (princ)
)
```

---
---
guid: GUID-94A0EA14-5165-4D84-A2F1-F44D33F80BCC
title: "FAQ: Why Don't My Custom Images Display with A Transparent Color?"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-8EF0EF11-D9F8-45F2-8870-48F0CC82BCD7
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-94A0EA14-5165-4D84-A2F1-F44D33F80BCC.htm
---

1. In an image editor external to the AutoCAD-based product, open the BMP file that was created to use the color 192,192,192 for transparency.
2. In the image editor, set a drawing tool current and specify the current color as transparent.
3. In the image editor window, change the pixels currently assigned the color 192,192,192 to the transparent color.
4. Save the image as a PNG file.
5. In the AutoCAD-based product, at the Command prompt, enter
   .
6. In the CUI Editor, assign the PNG file to the command which was previously assigned the original BMP file.
7. Save the changes made in the CUI Editor.

---
guid: GUID-97BB042C-BB33-4C42-8122-8765A9401B6A
title: "About Invoking an Object’s Method (AutoLISP/ActiveX)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-A0459510-CE7A-4206-9EAA-E25AAB569B20
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-97BB042C-BB33-4C42-8122-8765A9401B6A.htm
---

* A VLA-object identifying the object whose method you want to invoke
* Any additional arguments to make a valid call with the method

```
(setq MSpace (vla-get-ModelSpace (vla-get-ActiveDocument (vlax-get-acad-object))))
#<VLA-OBJECT IAcadModelSpace 0000000030434638>

(vla-AddCircle MSpace (vlax-3d-point '(5.0 5.0 0.0)) 3)
#<VLA-OBJECT IAcadCircle 00000000303b2698>
```

* A VLA-object identifying the object whose method you want to invoke
* A symbol or string naming the method to invoke
* Any additional arguments to make a valid call with the method

```
(setq MSpace (vlax-get-property (vlax-get-property (vlax-get-acad-object) 'ActiveDocument) 'ModelSpace))
#<VLA-OBJECT IAcadModelSpace 0000000030434638>

(vlax-invoke-method MSpace 'AddCircle (vlax-3d-point '(5.0 5.0 0.0)) 3)
#<VLA-OBJECT IAcadCircle 00000000303b2698>
```

---
---
guid: GUID-986313E1-0AEB-41DA-BC8B-093437F42B6A
title: "About Safearrays (AutoLISP/ActiveX)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-697D55E3-BEED-41BF-A974-E65614B912AE
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-986313E1-0AEB-41DA-BC8B-093437F42B6A.htm
---

* Integer
* Long integer
* Single-precision floating-point number
* Double-precision floating-point number
* String
* Object
* Boolean
* Variant

```
(setq point (vlax-make-safearray vlax-vbDouble '(0 . 2)))
#<safearray...>
```

```
(setq mat2 (vlax-make-safearray vlax-vbString '(0 . 1) '(1 . 3)))
#<safearray...>
```

* – Stores data in the elements of a safearray.
* – Assigns a value to an element in a safearray.
* – Returns the data type of a safearray.
* – Returns the number of dimensions in a safearray.
* – Returns the lower boundary (first index) of a dimension in a safearray.
* – Returns the upper boundary (last index) of a dimension in a safearray.
* – Returns the value for an element in a safearray.

---
guid: GUID-9985B23D-C42D-431D-B766-D1E5FE3ECC07
title: "About Creating and Managing CAD Standards"
depth: 3
parent_guid: GUID-E4499CB3-3CF1-48BE-93C9-1133E2D29434
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-9985B23D-C42D-431D-B766-D1E5FE3ECC07.htm
---

* Named objects in a drawing, which include layers, text styles, dimension styles, linetypes, and so on
* Title and detail blocks
* Annotation guidelines and methods
* Drawing layout and sheet set guidelines
* Object property conventions (ByLayer, ByBlock, or explicitly set)

* – Edits the objects within a block contained in a drawing, such as a detail or title block. (BEDIT command)
* – Exports selected objects or a block from a drawing to a new drawing (DWG) file. (WBLOCK command)
* – Creates and manages layers in a drawing. (LAYER command)
* – Creates and manages text styles in a drawing. (STYLE command)
* – Creates and manages dimension styles in a drawing. (DIMSTYLE command)
* – Imports and manages linetypes in a drawing. (LINETYPE command)
* – Creates and manages multileader styles in a drawing. (MLEADERSTYLE command)
* – Creates and manages multiline styles in a drawing. (MLSTYLE command)
* – Creates and manages table styles in a drawing. (TABLESTYLE command)
* – Creates and manages detail view styles in a drawing. (VIEWDETAILTSTYLE command)
* – Creates and manages section view styles in a drawing. (VIEWSECTIONSTYLE command)
* – Creates and manages layouts in a drawing. (LAYOUT command)
* – Drawing files that contain established named objects, title and detail blocks, and other information that are used to create new drawings. Drawing templates have a file extension of . and are created using the SAVEAS command.
* – Imports named objects from another drawing into the current drawing. (ADCENTER command)
* – Merges layers and changes the properties of layers in a drawing based on a layer mapping table. (LAYTRANS command)
* – Checks for and fixes standards violations in the current drawing against those defined in a drawing standards (DWS) file. (STANDARDS command)
* – Checks for standards violations in selected drawing files against those defined in a drawing standards (DWS) file.

---
---
guid: GUID-9B00D0C1-AC01-4519-BC90-339AF2120219
title: "About Compiler Modes (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-B5390E1B-3279-4B86-87D8-09D5EE958500
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-9B00D0C1-AC01-4519-BC90-339AF2120219.htm
---

* Standard build mode - Produces the smallest output file and is suitable for programs consisting of a single file.
* Optimize and link indirectly - Optimizes the compiled files, but does not create direct references to the compiled functions in the compiled code.
* Optimize and link directly - Optimizes the compiled files and creates direct references to the compiled function in the compiled code, instead of to the function symbol.

* Link function calls to create direct references to the compiled function in the compiled code, instead of to the function symbol. This feature improves the performance of the compiled code and protects the code against function redefinition at runtime.
* Drop function names to make the compiled code more secure and to decrease program size and load time.
* Drop the names of all local variables and directly link their references. This also makes the compiled code more secure and decreases program size and load time.

parent_guid: GUID-209318DE-95C4-40F6-8776-935C8905FDEE
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Tutorials/files/GUID-9E5E5FA3-7277-4245-8993-86E24F94991A.htm

---
---
guid: GUID-9EBE2E26-F942-4305-BDE4-D6D479DD09A8
title: "To Set Up a Paradox Data Source Using ODBC"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-1C006BB3-9909-420B-B5D7-791E2B104C46
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-9EBE2E26-F942-4305-BDE4-D6D479DD09A8.htm
---

1. Click the Windows Start button Windows System Control Panel.
2. Double-click the Administrative Tools icon, and then double-click Data Sources (ODBC).
3. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, do one of the following:
   * Click the User DSN tab to create a data source that is visible only to you and can be used only on the computer you create it in.
   * Click the System DSN tab to create a data source that is visible to all users who have access rights to the computer.
   * Click the File DSN tab to create a data source that can be shared with other users who have the same ODBC drivers installed on their systems.
4. Click Add.
5. Select the Paradox Driver, and then click Finish.
6. Enter a name for your data source in Data Source Name, and select the appropriate version of Paradox from the Version list.
7. Make sure that User Current Directory is cleared.
8. Click Select Directory, and then locate and select the database you want to configure. Click OK.
9. In the ODBC Paradox Setup dialog box, click OK.
10. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, click OK.

guid: GUID-9F2F672F-F9AF-4435-A481-52FE13540B08
title: "To Create a Submenu on a Menu"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-D4B7B53A-975D-437E-A906-DD15A557B82F
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-9F2F672F-F9AF-4435-A481-52FE13540B08.htm
---

1. Click
   .
2. In the Customize tab, Customizations In
   pane, click the plus sign (+) next to the Menus node to expand it.
3. Select the menu you want to add a submenu to.
4. Right-click the menu. Click New Sub-menu.
5. Right-click Menu1. Click Rename and enter a new submenu name.
6. In the Properties pane, Description box, optionally enter a description for the submenu.
7. In the Command List pane, drag the command that you want to add to the submenu in the Customizations In
   pane.
8. Continue adding commands until the new submenu is complete.
9. Click Apply.

---
---
guid: GUID-A42448EB-3E46-4902-9980-255DBA1EF9CB
title: "Example: Convert Inches to Meters (AutoLISP)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-8256416C-3302-4BBF-B4C9-98A7973FBC96
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-A42448EB-3E46-4902-9980-255DBA1EF9CB.htm
---

```
(defun C:I2M ( / eng_len metric_len eng metric)
  (princ "\nConverting inches to meters. ")
  (setq eng_len
  (getdist "\nEnter a distance in inches: "))
  (setq metric_len (cvunit eng_len "inches" "meters"))
  (setq eng (rtos eng_len 2 4)
           metric (rtos metric_len 2 4))
  (princ
    (strcat "\n\t" eng " inches = " metric " meters."))
 (princ)
)
```

guid: GUID-A61FAC68-AAA4-4242-9349-811071D53DA4
title: "To set and retrieve variables from a document namespace (AutoLISP)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-914D27BD-60F2-47E6-BF28-310AD365F783
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-A61FAC68-AAA4-4242-9349-811071D53DA4.htm
---

1. At the AutoCAD Command prompt or in an AutoLISP program, enter an AutoLISP statement that uses the function and press Enter.
2. Enter the name of the variable you assigned a value to and prefix it with an (exclamation point) to return the value assigned to the variable and press Enter.

---
guid: GUID-A63E8C40-6870-4874-BF7E-FD75E87268AA
title: "To Digitally Sign an AutoLISP File"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-0A93626D-8389-45FC-969B-B86A2F37D691
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-A63E8C40-6870-4874-BF7E-FD75E87268AA.htm
---

1. Click the Windows Start button Autodesk Attach Digital Signatures.
2. In the Attach Digital Signatures dialog box, click Add Files.
3. In the Select File dialog box, browse to and select the AutoLISP file to digitally sign. Click Open.
4. In the Attach Digital Signatures dialog box, under the Select A Digital ID (Certificate) section, select a digital ID.
5. Under the Signature Information section, click the Get Time Stamp From drop-down list and select a server or the local computer.
6. Optionally, in the Comment text box, enter a description as to why the file is being digitally signed.
7. Click Sign Files.
8. In the Signing Complete message box, click OK.
9. In the Attach Digital Signatures dialog box, sign additional files or click Close.
10. Load the newly signed file into an AutoCAD-based program or AutoCAD LT, and verify that the digital signature is recognized.

guid: GUID-A694AB72-7EB7-4560-B473-B480C378E457
title: "About Multiple Configurations"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-C9217007-3B3D-48AE-96BA-07378EC927F6
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-A694AB72-7EB7-4560-B473-B480C378E457.htm

---
---
guid: GUID-A6AFD973-4196-4000-8541-6D5852D006E2
title: "Visual LISP Related File Extensions (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-7D8E6EF3-8BFD-4BBC-BB86-0AE21244ACE7
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-A6AFD973-4196-4000-8541-6D5852D006E2.htm
---

* – Backup files; Backup copies of edited files, maintained by the Visual LISP editor. Backup files contain the same name as the original, except that the file extension begins with the underline character (\_) and is followed by the first two characters of the original file's extension. For example, the backup file of a LSP file has an .\_LS extension; the backup of a DCL file has a .\_DC extension.
* – Language source files; Contain program source code. The Visual LISP editor recognizes the syntax of these files and color-codes reserved words, strings, and numbers.
* – Dialog control language; Contains definitions of AutoCAD dialog boxes. Visual LISP can preview these files, and you can include them in Visual LISP executable (VLX) files.
* – Desktop save; Contains Visual LISP environment and window settings. (Note: Editing this file may permanently change the Visual LISP environment. Do not edit this file without creating a backup copy first.)
* – Compiled AutoLISP program; May be loaded and ran, or compiled into VLX files.
* – AutoLISP source code; Program source files that can be loaded and ran, or compiled into FAS or VLX files.
* – Object code; Used internally by Visual LISP, these files contain compiled AutoLISP code used in building FAS files.
* – Project database; Used internally by Visual LISP, these files contain symbol information used by the compiler.
* – Project definition; Contains the location and names of all source files that build the project, as well as certain parameters and rules on how to create the final FAS files.
* – Make application; Defines the files and options used to build a VLX application with the Visual LISP Make Application wizard.
* – Structured query language; Contains SQL statements. The Visual LISP text editor recognizes this file type and color-codes the text according to SQL syntax rules.
* – Stand-alone applications; Stand-alone AutoCAD applications, which can be created using the Visual LISP Make Application wizard.

---

title: "Frame Binding Window Shortcut Menu Reference (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 7
parent_guid: GUID-C8278A71-D172-4511-AC38-A238462D532C
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-A77C0C6B-EBCE-41BC-8C99-D3467C8B3679.htm

---
guid: GUID-A7842E65-0BF1-4D41-9CCA-05AFA5AACF10
title: "To Set Up a DBase Data Source Using ODBC"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-1C006BB3-9909-420B-B5D7-791E2B104C46
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-A7842E65-0BF1-4D41-9CCA-05AFA5AACF10.htm
---

1. Click the Windows Start button Windows System Control Panel.
2. Double-click the Administrative Tools icon, and then double-click Data Sources (ODBC).
3. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, do one of the following:
   * Click the User DSN tab to create a data source that is visible only to you and can be used only on the computer you create it in.
   * Click the System DSN tab to create a data source that is visible to all users who have access rights to the computer.
   * Click the File DSN tab to create a data source that can be shared with other users who have the same ODBC drivers installed on their systems.
4. Click Add.
5. Select the Microsoft dBase Driver, and then click Finish.
6. Enter a name for your data source in Data Source Name, and select the appropriate version of dBase from the Version list.
7. Make sure that Use Current Directory is cleared.
8. Click Select Directory, and then locate and select the directory that contains the database tables you want to configure. Click OK.
9. In the ODBC dBase Setup dialog box, click OK.
10. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, click OK.

---
---
guid: GUID-A79A1D4D-585A-4736-8905-53CD74DD15FB
title: "Example: Accessing Drawing Properties (AutoLISP/ActiveX)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-50158F17-992B-4427-B64F-31EF77BECBD7
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-A79A1D4D-585A-4736-8905-53CD74DD15FB.htm
---

```
(vl-load-com)
(defun c:ADD_PROPS (/ doc db si author nc nc2 nc3 value3 value4)
  (setq doc (vla-get-ActiveDocument (vlax-get-Acad-Object)))
  (setq db (vla-get-Database doc))
  (setq si (vla-get-SummaryInfo db))

  (vla-put-author si "John")
  (vla-put-comments si "New comments")
  (vla-put-hyperlinkbase si "https://www.autodesk.com")
  (vla-put-keywords si "New keywords")

  (vla-AddCustomInfo si "siPutKey" "siPutValue")

  (setq nc (vla-numcustominfo si))
  (vla-SetCustomByKey si "siPutKey" "siPutValueByKey")
  (vla-GetCustomByKey si "siPutKey" 'value3)

  (if (/= "siPutValueByKey" value3)
    (princ "*** Error SetCustomByKey\n")
  )

  (vla-SetCustomByIndex si (1- nc) "siPutCustomByIndexKey" "siPutCustomByIndexValue")
  (vla-GetCustomByKey si "siPutCustomByIndexKey" 'value4)

  (if (/= "siPutCustomByIndexValue" value4)
    (princ "*** Error SetCustomByIndex\n")
  )

  (vla-RemoveCustomByIndex si (1- nc))

  (setq nc2 (vla-numcustominfo si))
  (if (/= nc2 (1- nc))
    (princ "*** Error RemoveCustomByIndex")
  )

  (vla-AddCustomInfo si "siPutKey" "siPutValue")

  ; Remove property
  (vla-RemoveCustomByKey si "siPutKey")
  (setq nc3 (vla-numcustominfo si))
  (if (/= nc2 (1- nc))
    (princ "*** Error RemoveCustomByKey")
  )

  (vla-AddCustomInfo si "siPutKey" "siPutValue")

  (vlax-release-object si)
  (vlax-release-object db)
  (vlax-release-object doc)
 (princ)
)
(princ)
```

```
(vl-load-com)
(defun c:GET_PROPS (/ doc db si author )
  (if (/= "MyDrawing.dwg" (getvar "DWGNAME"))
    (princ "Open MyDrawing.dwg")
    (progn
      (setq doc (vla-get-ActiveDocument (vlax-get-Acad-Object)))
      (setq db (vla-get-Database doc))
      (setq si (vla-get-SummaryInfo db))

      (princ "\nAuthor: \n")
      (if (/= "John" (setq author (vla-get-author si)))
        (princ "*** vla-get-author error")
        (princ author)
      )
      (princ "\n")
      (princ "\nComments:\n ")
      (princ (vla-get-comments si))
      (princ "\n")
      (princ "\nHyperlink-base: \n")
      (princ (vla-get-HyperlinkBase si))
      (princ "\n")
      (princ "\nNumber of custom properties: ")
      (princ (setq nc (vla-numcustominfo si)))
      (princ "\n")
      (while (> nc 0)
        (princ "Custom property ")
        (princ nc)
        (vla-GetCustomByIndex si (- nc 1) 'key 'value)
        (princ ": key(")
        (princ key)
        (princ ")")
        (princ " value(")
        (princ value)
        (princ ")\n")
        (vla-GetCustomByKey si key 'value2)
        (if (/= value value2)
          (princ "\n*** Error GetCustomByKey returned unexpected result.\n")
        )
        (setq nc (1- nc))
      )
      (vlax-release-object si)
      (vlax-release-object db)
      (vlax-release-object doc)
    )
  )
 (princ)
)
```

---
guid: GUID-A7D0E518-D72F-474E-A97E-89CC56A7ADBD
title: "About Manually Migrating Custom Settings From Previous Releases"
depth: 2
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-A7D0E518-D72F-474E-A97E-89CC56A7ADBD.htm
---

* . All user profiles in the previous release are migrated. If you do not want to migrate all user profiles, use the Profiles tab in the Options dialog box to export each profile from the previous release and import those profiles that were exported into the current release. (User Profiles are not available in AutoCAD LT.)
* . The Migrate Custom Settings utility migrates the MNU, MNS, CUI, or CUIx files associated with the user profiles from the previous release; the file is specified under the Main Customization File setting. The customization files are migrated to the current release and the identified changes to the customization files that shipped with the previous release are merged with the file of the same name in the current release, as needed. While the Migrate Custom Settings utility does not migrate the CUIx file specified under the Enterprise Customization File node setting, the reference to the file is migrated to the current release.
* . The Migrate Custom Settings utility merges the changes made to the linetype (LIN), hatch pattern (PAT), and program parameter (PGP) files that shipped with the previous release with the files of the same name in the current release. If you do not want all the changes made to these files, you will need to edit each file individually using an ASCII text editor.
* . The Migrate Custom Settings utility can migrate both tool palettes and tool palette groups to the current release. User-defined tool palette files are copied to the current release and the changes to tool palette files that shipped with AutoCAD 2010-based products or later are merged with the tool palette files of the same name in the current release. If migrating from an AutoCAD 2009-based products or earlier, only user-created tool palettes are migrated; changes made to the tool palettes that shipped with the product must be recreated. Along with the migration of tool palettes, user-defined tool palette groups are migrated from the previous release to the current release.

---

guid: GUID-A9477324-6F95-4210-8DCD-3A955C027AA8
title: "To Configure a Xerox HDI Plotter Driver "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-5557B70A-CAF8-43D6-B7B7-80FEF17235FA
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-A9477324-6F95-4210-8DCD-3A955C027AA8.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the Add-a-Plotter Wizard shortcut icon.
3. On the Begin page, select My Computer if the plotter is connected to your computer. Select Network Plotter Server if the plotter is available through a network. Click Next.
4. On the Network Plotter page, enter the UNC name of the networked plotter. Click Next.
5. On the Plotter Model page under Manufacturers, select Xerox Engineering Systems. Under Model, select the type of Xerox plotter that you are using. Click Next.
6. On the Import PCP or PC2 page, click Next to continue.
7. On the Ports page, select the port that the printer is attached to. Click Next.
8. On the Plotter Name page, enter a name for the plotter configuration file. Click Next.
9. On the Finish page, click Finish.

guid: GUID-AC091479-5579-4EBE-823D-898160592E5B
title: "To Configure an HP-GL/2 Plotter Driver "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-93357112-AC38-4E1F-B35C-79369388BA1D
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-AC091479-5579-4EBE-823D-898160592E5B.htm
---

1. click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the Add-a-Plotter Wizard shortcut icon.
3. On the Begin page, select My Computer if the plotter is connected to your computer. Select Network Plotter Server if the plotter is available through a network. Click Next.
4. On the Network Plotter page, enter the UNC name of the networked plotter. Click Next.
5. On the Plotter Model page under Manufacturers, select Hewlett-Packard. Under Model, select the type of Hewlett-Packard plotter that you are using or emulating. Click Next.
6. On the Import PCP or PC2 page, click Next to continue.
7. On the Ports page, select the port that the printer is attached to. Click Next.
8. On the Plotter Name page, enter a name for the plotter configuration file. Click Next.

guid: GUID-AC5C2A9B-0D09-4E97-8E53-2B4F68DECAB8
title: "To Create a PC3 File for a Windows System Printer"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-D1786BA2-1CB1-4585-AA6A-6ED8088D4B28

4. On the Add Plotter - Begin page, click System Printer. Click Next.
5. On the Add Plotter - System Printer page, select the system printer that you want to configure.
6. On the Import PCP or PC2 page, click Next to continue.
7. On the Add Plotter - Plotter Name page, enter a name to identify the currently configured plotter. Click Next.
8. When you reach the Add Plotter - Finish page, you can click Finish to exit the Add-a-Plotter wizard.

guid: GUID-AD027505-9C7C-4DEE-84A7-4E90C8129E63
title: "To Create or Edit a Button Image "
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-110030E5-F82E-4920-BF47-AEFF483CF196
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-AD027505-9C7C-4DEE-84A7-4E90C8129E63.htm
---

1. Click
   .
2. In the Customize tab, Command List or Customizations In
   pane, select a command to display the Button Image pane.
3. In the Button Image pane, select an image from the Image list that is closest in appearance to the image you want to create or select an existing image to edit. Click Edit.
4. In the Button Editor dialog box, use the Pencil, Line, Circle, and Erase tools to create or edit the button image. To change the working color, select a color from the color palette, or click More to open the Select Color dialog box.
   * . Applies the selected color to one of the squares on the canvas. Each square represents one pixel. You can drag the pointing device to edit several squares at once.
   * . Creates lines in the selected color. Click, drag and release to draw lines.
   * . Creates circles or ovals in the selected color. Click, drag and release to create circles or ovals.
   * Resets the color of one square of the canvas to the default color.
5. Click Save.
6. In the Save Image dialog box, Image Name box, enter a name and click OK.
7. Click Close.
8. Click Apply.

guid: GUID-AD10051A-822B-4E94-A615-F2A074E878C5
title: "About Expressions (AutoLISP)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-0365EB64-531D-4CC0-B740-E756CC5E5AB6
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-AD10051A-822B-4E94-A615-F2A074E878C5.htm
---

```
(function )
```

* Begins with an open (left) parenthesis.
* Consists of a function name and optional arguments for that function. Each argument can also be an expression.
* Ends with a close (right) parenthesis.
* Returns a value that can be used by a surrounding expression. The value of the last interpreted expression is returned to the calling expression.

```
(fun1 (fun2 )(fun3 ))
```

```

54
```

```

30
```

```

30
```

title: "About Compiler Optimizing Conditions (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-E3D8A54C-ADB6-46A7-BD00-4E9409030282
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-AE9F0D0B-CE7C-4822-8F1A-708CCAB3CCCE.htm
---



---
---
guid: GUID-AEC3C9EF-4987-4153-A7F8-B3A0662D4CCA
title: "About Fixing the Spacing Around a Boxed Row or Column (DCL)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-24D6CEDA-B771-4F1E-9ADD-F1BF4CB21608
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-AEC3C9EF-4987-4153-A7F8-B3A0662D4CCA.htm
---

* If the label is a single blank, any vertical space the text occupied inside the box is lost, but any vertical space the label occupied above the box is not lost.
* If the label is a null string, all vertical space is lost, whether above the box or inside it.

```
: row {
  : boxed_column {
    label = "Some Text";
  }
  : boxed_column {
    label = " ";         // single blank: the default
  }
  : boxed_column {
    label = "";          // null string
  }
}
```

guid: GUID-B140BF54-AD94-47EE-BC3E-91AEFA63D0CE
title: "About Importing a Type Library (AutoLISP/ActiveX)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-7D4E0D6B-5714-4D2F-B124-545FCB3EFD75
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-B140BF54-AD94-47EE-BC3E-91AEFA63D0CE.htm
---

```
(vlax-import-type-library :tlb-filename  [ :methods-prefix  :properties-prefix  :constants-prefix ])
```

* want your code to run on different machines, avoid specifying an absolute path in the
  parameter.
* If possible, avoid using
  from inside any AutoLISP expression (in other words, always call it from a top-level position).
* In your AutoLISP source file, code the
  call before any code that uses method or property wrappers or constants defined in the type library.

---
guid: GUID-B18A6E87-2CD1-4303-81C8-375095DB5D81
title: "To Set Up a Microsoft Access Data Source Using ODBC"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-1C006BB3-9909-420B-B5D7-791E2B104C46
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-B18A6E87-2CD1-4303-81C8-375095DB5D81.htm
---

1. Click the Windows Start button Windows System Control Panel.
2. Double-click the Administrative Tools icon, and then double-click Data Sources (ODBC).
3. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, do one of the following:
   * Click the User DSN tab to create a data source that is visible only to you and can be used only on the computer you create it in.
   * Click the System DSN tab to create a data source that is visible to all users who have access rights to the computer.
   * Click the File DSN tab to create a data source that can be shared with other users who have the same ODBC drivers installed on their systems.
4. Click Add.
5. Select the Microsoft Access Driver, and then click Finish.
6. Enter a name for your data source in Data Source Name.
7. Click Select, and then locate and select the database that you want to configure. Click OK.
8. In the ODBC Microsoft Access dialog box, click OK.
9. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, click OK.

---

guid: GUID-B18FA64E-AF62-4399-9D4F-57A18A472185
title: "To Download and Install VS Code "
depth: 4

---

1. Launch your Web browser and browse to
   .
2. On the Visual Studio Code page, click Download and then choose the download specific to your platform.
3. After you download the VS Code installer, start the installer and follow the on-screen instructions.

guid: GUID-B42E7914-A228-4CCF-98BF-FFD41B35BB97
title: "To Set Color Depth for Plotted DWF Files"
depth: 7
parent_guid: GUID-232B462B-9804-425D-AB19-024E4772DA65
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-B42E7914-A228-4CCF-98BF-FFD41B35BB97.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print.
2. In the Printer/Plotter area, in the Name list, select a DWF plotting device. Click Properties.
3. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, Device and Document Settings tab, expand the Graphics node in the tree window.
4. Click Vector Graphics.
5. In the Color Depth area, select a color depth. Click OK.
6. In the Changes to a Printer Configuration dialog box, do one of the following. Then click OK.
   * Select Apply Changes for the Current Plot Only to specify a one-time override of the configuration settings that is not saved to the DWF configuration file.
   * Select Save Changes to the Following File to save the configuration changes to the DWF configuration file.
7. In the Browse for Plot File dialog box, in the Save In location list, select a plotting location for the DWF file, and click Save. Click OK.

guid: GUID-B682DF97-DFD5-48B4-9FFF-8A0DF7CAC05F
title: "About Handling Errors in a VLX Application Running in Its Own Namespace (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-E6818F46-FAFA-4D1C-B584-40DD598E0AC0

---

```
(defun *error* (msg)
  ... ; processing in VLX namespace/execution context
(vl-exit-with-error (strcat "My application bombed! " msg)))
```

```
(defun *error* (msg)
  ... ; processing in VLX-T namespace/execution context
  (vl-exit-with-value  3))
(vl-doc-export 'foo)
(defun foo (x)
  (bar x)
  (print 3))
(defun bar (x) (list (/ 2 x) x))
```

---
guid: GUID-B6FD0211-23FA-4F65-80EE-142B2BC2E188
title: "About Defining Callback Functions (AutoLISP/ActiveX)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-49DB4EF4-7386-42CC-9633-5ABCDFA9D5D9
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-B6FD0211-23FA-4F65-80EE-142B2BC2E188.htm
---

* The first argument identifies the Reactor object that called the function.
* The second argument is a list of parameters set by AutoCAD.

```
(defun saveDrawingInfo (calling-reactor commandInfo / dwgname filesize)
  (vl-load-com)
  (setq dwgname (cadr commandInfo)
    filesize (vl-file-size dwgname)
  )
  (alert (strcat "The file size of " dwgname " is "
      (itoa filesize) " bytes."
    )
  )
 (princ)
)
```

* - Simple function that makes a beep from your workstation’s speakers.
* - Prints a list of arguments to the Visual LISP Trace window each time a reactor fires this callback function.

---
---
guid: GUID-B8474359-5A37-4094-8D8C-1C2EA2D6F43E
title: "About Checking the Balance of Parentheses (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-13E81F52-B89D-4CF6-B57D-8E404CEC14D9
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-B8474359-5A37-4094-8D8C-1C2EA2D6F43E.htm
---

```
  (defun yinyang (/ origin radius i-radius half-r origin-x origin-y)
  (setq half-r (/ radius 2))
  (setq origin-x (car origin))
  (setq origin-y (cadr origin))
  (command "._circle" 
           origin 
           radius
           (command "._arc"
                    "_c"
                   (list origin-x (+ origin-y half-r)) 
                   (list origin-x (+ origin-y radius)) 
                   origin                             
          )
          (command "._arc"
                   "_c"
                  (list origin-x (- origin-y half-r)) 
                  (list origin-x (- origin-y radius)) 
                  origin                             
          )
 )
```

* Visual LISP does not find a matching close parenthesis, so the cursor does not move.
* Move the cursor to the beginning of line 2.
* Cursor moves to the end of line 2.
* Cursor moves to the end of line 3.
* Cursor moves to the end of line 4.
* Cursor jumps to the last right parenthesis in the program which is on line 20.

url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-B8D310FC-4AA5-4C04-8DC3-8646E05DEF34.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print.
2. In the Printer/Plotter area, in the Name list, select a DWF plotting device. Click Properties.
3. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, Device and Document Settings tab, select Custom Properties from the tree window.
4. In the Access Custom Dialog area, click Custom Properties.
5. In the DWF6 ePlot Properties dialog box, in the Font Handling area, select a font capture option. Click OK.
6. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, click OK.
7. In the Changes to a Printer Configuration dialog box, do one of the following. Then click OK.
   * Select Apply Changes for the Current Plot Only to specify a one-time override of the configuration settings that is not saved to the DWF configuration file.
   * Select Save Changes to the Following File to save the configuration changes to the DWF configuration file.
8. In the Browse for Plot File dialog box, in the Save In location list, select a plotting location for the DWF file, and click Save. Click OK.

guid: GUID-B9F4F365-8FE5-453C-B8E3-72D3CBCF304C
title: "To Set Up a Direct Oracle Configuration Using OLE DB"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-1C006BB3-9909-420B-B5D7-791E2B104C46
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-B9F4F365-8FE5-453C-B8E3-72D3CBCF304C.htm
---

1. At the Command prompt, enter .
2. On the dbConnect Manager, right-click Data Sources and click Configure Data Source.
3. In the Configure a Data Source dialog box, do one of the following:
   * In the Data Source Name box, enter a name for the data source. Click OK.
   * In the Data Sources list box, select a data source. Click OK.
4. In the Data Link Properties dialog box, Provider tab, select Microsoft OLE DB Provider for Oracle. Click Next.
5. In the Select or Enter a Server Name box, enter the Oracle server name.
6. In the User Name and Password boxes, enter a valid user name and password.
7. Click Test Connection to verify that the settings are correct.
8. Click OK.

guid: GUID-BA488DA2-20A1-430F-8F50-06AF850EBE00
title: "To create an object reactor (AutoLISP/ActiveX)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-396A2538-4C9E-4A12-8174-289A13F6E208
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-BA488DA2-20A1-430F-8F50-06AF850EBE00.htm
---

1. Determine which object event to use for the reactor.
2. Define the function that will be used as the callback for the reactor.
3. Define the function that creates or gets the VLA-object in which you want to attach the reactor.
4. Create the reactor; statement that creates the reactor object, assigns application-specific data, associates which VLA-objects that the reactor should work with, and specifies the callback function.
5. Load, run, and test the AutoLISP code.

* The first argument identifies the object that fired the notification.
* The second argument identifies the Reactor object that called the function.
* The third argument is a list of parameters specific to the callback condition.

```
(defun print-radius (notifier-object reactor-object parameter-list)
  (vl-load-com)
  (cond
    (
      (vlax-property-available-p
        notifier-object
        "Radius"
      )
      (princ "The radius is ")
      (princ (vla-get-radius notifier-object))
    )
  )
)
```

guid: GUID-BF30AA6B-AB31-4085-BEC8-ABA518E9DD3C
title: "About Modifying Selection Sets (AutoLISP)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-7BE77062-C359-4D01-915B-69CF672C653B
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-BF30AA6B-AB31-4085-BEC8-ABA518E9DD3C.htm
---

```
(setq fname (entnext))                 ; Gets first entity in the drawing.
(setq lname (entlast))                 ; Gets last entity in the drawing.
(if (not fname)
  (princ "\nNo entities in drawing. ")
  (progn
    (setq ourset (ssadd fname))        ; Creates a selection set 
                                       ; of the first entity.
    (ssadd lname ourset)               ; Adds the last entity to 
                                       ; the selection set.
  )
)
```

```
(ssdel fname ourset)
```

```
(setq sset (ssget))                     ; Prompts the user to create
                                        ; a selection set.
(setq ent1 (ssname sset 0))             ; Gets the name of the first
                                        ; entity in sset.
(setq ent4 (ssname sset 3))             ; Gets the name of the fourth
                                        ; entity in sset.
(if (not ent4)
  (princ "\nNeed to select at least four entities. ")
)
(setq ilast (sslength sset))            ; Finds index of the last
                                        ; entity in sset.
                                        ; Gets the name of the last
                                        ; entity in sset.
(setq lastent (ssname sset (1- ilast)))
```

title: "To Configure an HP-GL Plotter Driver "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-5B7D0D2E-A89D-4735-87FB-94B961F88A73
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-C20BE46F-9EC6-4F4F-BA97-52286EC7D19B.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the Add-a-Plotter Wizard shortcut icon.
3. On the Begin page, select My Computer if the plotter is connected to your computer. Select Network Plotter Server if the plotter is available through a network. Click Next.
4. On the Network Plotter page, enter the UNC name of the networked plotter. Click Next.
5. On the Plotter Model page, under Manufacturers, select Hewlett-Packard. Under Model, select the type of Hewlett-Packard plotter that you are using or emulating. Click Next.
6. On the Import PCP or PC2 page, click Next to continue.
7. On the Ports page, select the port that the printer is attached to. Click Next.
8. On the Plotter Name page, enter a name for the plotter configuration file. Click Next.
9. On the Finish page, click Finish.

title: "About Using the Console Window History (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-CBBC571C-6691-4B45-BAA5-DB48A322870A
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-C2DD109E-A90A-43EC-A620-3C2A582EF7A6.htm
---



---
---
guid: GUID-C2F7FF00-0EF3-4EAC-A062-4C2E8EEFA985
title: "To Add a Simple Linetype to an LIN File"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-EF1DF0A9-2088-487C-8085-16FEE6425405
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-C2F7FF00-0EF3-4EAC-A062-4C2E8EEFA985.htm
---

1. Open an LIN file in a text editor that saves in ASCII format (for example, Notepad on Windows or TextEdit on Mac OS).
2. Create a header line that includes an asterisk and a linetype pattern name. The name of the linetype pattern is limited to 31 characters.

   ```
   *BORDER,Border
   ```
3. (Optional) Include a description on the header line, follow the linetype pattern name with a comma and description text.

   ```
   *BORDER,Border __ __ . __ __ . __ __ . __ __ . __ __ .
   ```
4. Create a descriptor line that follows these rules:
   * All linetypes must begin with a dash.
   * Enter zeros for dots.
   * Enter negative real numbers for spaces. The value defines the length of the space in drawing units.
   * Enter positive real numbers for dashes. The value defines the length of the dash in drawing units.
   * Separate each dot, dash, or space value from the next with a comma.
   * Use a space between a dot and a dash.

   ```
   A,.5,-.25,.5,-.25,0,-.25
   ```

guid: GUID-C38EF8C9-186E-47CE-AAE8-0C130D5330A6

parent_guid: GUID-732CEDF8-4005-444C-8BA9-809E352B27EE

guid: GUID-C5F1E0AF-CAE8-4338-8C27-5A4235D37145
title: " textpage (AutoLISP)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-C5F1E0AF-CAE8-4338-8C27-5A4235D37145.htm

---
---
guid: GUID-C60E0AE4-DB9A-4A34-B704-79CD7DF60B65
title: "To Set Up an SQL Server Data Source Using ODBC"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-1C006BB3-9909-420B-B5D7-791E2B104C46
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-C60E0AE4-DB9A-4A34-B704-79CD7DF60B65.htm
---

1. Click the Windows Start button Windows System Control Panel.
2. Double-click the Administrative Tools icon, and then double-click Data Sources (ODBC).
3. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, do one of the following:
   * Click the User DSN tab to create a data source that is visible only to you and can be used only on the computer you create it in.
   * Click the System DSN tab to create a data source that is visible to all users who have access rights to the computer.
   * Click the File DSN tab to create a data source that can be shared with other users who have the same ODBC drivers installed on their systems.
4. Click Add.
5. Select SQL Server, and then click Finish.
6. Follow the instructions in the wizard to complete the data source setup.
7. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, click OK.

---
guid: GUID-C9A09267-3877-478E-BC3C-0A6C8F2F17FD
title: "To Make Functions in a Separate-namespace VLX Available to Other VLX Applications (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 7
parent_guid: GUID-6439354D-BC69-4DFE-971F-ED8AA9907AAB
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-C9A09267-3877-478E-BC3C-0A6C8F2F17FD.htm
---

1. In a Visual LISP text editor window, enter the AutoLISP statements the functionality you want to create.
2. Save the program file you created.
3. Build an application file using the Make Application wizard.
4. Load the VLX application file into AutoCAD.
5. Create another program that uses the function from the other VLX file.
6. Save the program file you created.
7. Build an application file using the Make Application wizard.
8. Load the VLX application file into AutoCAD and execute the function that utilizes the exported function.

(setq pgpname "acad.pgp")

title: "To Customize a Ribbon Contextual Tab State "
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-46187AC0-F25B-4A19-8E95-1722D780596F

---
---
guid: GUID-CD2F90E8-B8A4-4FE4-99A2-65B4C7D5837B
title: "To Set Color Depth for Plotted DWFx Files"
depth: 8
parent_guid: GUID-AD5DF835-6D1B-48E8-B745-0DF6A979B086
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-CD2F90E8-B8A4-4FE4-99A2-65B4C7D5837B.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print.
2. In the Printer/Plotter area, in the Name list, select a DWFx plotter configuration file. Click Properties.
3. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, click the Device and Document Settings tab.
4. Click the (+) sign to expand the Graphics node in the tree window.
5. Click Vector Graphics.
6. In the Color Depth area, select a color depth. Click OK.
7. In the Changes to a Printer Configuration dialog box, do one of the following:
   * Select Apply Changes for the Current Plot Only — to specify a one-time override of the configuration settings that is not saved to the DWF configuration file.
   * Select Save Changes to the Following File — to save the configuration changes to the DWF configuration file.
8. Click OK.
9. In the Browse for Plot File dialog box, navigate to the folder location you want to save. Click Save.

---
guid: GUID-CDEDEE51-76B1-4295-9F16-B2AD811C0EA6
title: "Example: Hiding a Dialog Box (DCL)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-828682DC-C82E-43C4-BB69-E1A6CBB0A461
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-CDEDEE51-76B1-4295-9F16-B2AD811C0EA6.htm
---

```
hidedcl : dialog
{
  label="Hide Example";
  : column
  {
    : text
    {
      key="message";
      label="Click PickMe to pick a point";
      fixed_width=true;
      fixed_height=true;
      alignment=centered;
    }
    :row
    {
      ok_only;
      :retirement_button
      {
        label = "PickMe";
        key = "hide";
        mnemonic = "H";
      }
    }
  }
}
```

```
(defun c:hidedcl (/ dcl_id what_next cnt)
  (setq dcl_id (load_dialog "hidedcl.dcl"))  ; Load the dialog box.
  (setq what_next 2)
  (setq cnt 1)
  (while (>= what_next 2)                    ; Begin display loop.
    (if (null (new_dialog "hidedcl" dcl_id)) ; Initialize dialog
      (exit)                                 ; box, exit if nil
    ) ; endif                                ; returned.

    ; Set action to take if a button is pressed. Either button
    ; results in a done_dialog call to close the dialog box.
    ; Each button associates a specific status code with
    ; done_dialog, and this status code is returned by
    ; start_dialog.
    (action_tile "accept" "(done_dialog 1)") ; Set action for OK.
    (action_tile "hide" "(done_dialog 4)")   ; Set action for PickMe.
    (setq what_next (start_dialog))          ; Display dialog box.

    (cond
      ((= what_next 4)                       ; Prompt user to
        (getpoint "\npick a point")          ; pick pt.
      )
      ((= what_next 0)
        (prompt "\nuser cancelled dialog")
      )
    )
  )
  (unload_dialog dcl_id)
 (princ)
)
```

guid: GUID-CF7E5870-561F-42DB-B134-CCD41EF93A25
title: " function (AutoLISP/Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 3
parent_guid: nan

---
---
guid: GUID-CF7EF516-C1F5-47A6-97A3-F1DB1B65E06C
title: "To Set Up an Oracle Data Source Using ODBC"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-1C006BB3-9909-420B-B5D7-791E2B104C46
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-CF7EF516-C1F5-47A6-97A3-F1DB1B65E06C.htm
---

1. Click the Windows Start button Windows System Control Panel.
2. Double-click the Administrative Tools icon, and then double-click Data Sources (ODBC).
3. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, do one of the following:
   * Click the User DSN tab to create a data source that is visible only to you and can be used only on the computer you create it in.
   * Click the System DSN tab to create a data source that is visible to all users who have access rights to the computer.
   * Click the File DSN tab to create a data source that can be shared with other users who have the same ODBC drivers installed on their systems.
4. Click Add.
5. Select Microsoft ODBC for Oracle, and then click Finish.
6. Enter a name for your data source in Data Source Name.
7. Enter your user name.
8. Enter the name of the Oracle Server in Server.
9. In the ODBC Microsoft Excel dialog box, click OK.
10. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, click OK.

url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-D029509F-A2A0-4A7E-BDD5-FE95E7235C5C.htm
---

* – Drawing files created with the command need to be opened and re-saved to an earlier file format as needed.
* – Drawing files edited with the command need to be opened and re-saved to an earlier file format as needed.
* and
  – Selected drawing objects are copied to a drawing file that is saved in the native drawing file format. You cannot copy and paste drawing objects between releases that use different native drawing file formats, such as AutoCAD 2017 and
  .
  + Use the WBLOCK command to export the selected objects to a separate drawing file.
  + Open the drawing file and re-save it to the earlier drawing file format with the SAVEAS command.
  + Bring the objects into the earlier release with the XREF or INSERT command.

* – A batch convertor that resaves selected drawing files between file formats.
* – A transmittal process that saves the current drawing and referenced drawing files to the selected drawing file format. The current Transmittal Setup controls the drawing file format to save the drawing to.
* – A stand-alone application that can be used to saves multiple drawing files to a specified file format. DWG TrueView is available as a separate and free download.
* – A batch script executor that runs specified script (SCR) files across selected drawing files. SCR files can be used to save drawings to a different file format. ()

---

guid: GUID-D03ABBC2-939A-44DB-8C93-FC63B64DE4A2
title: " rtos (AutoLISP)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-D03ABBC2-939A-44DB-8C93-FC63B64DE4A2.htm
