---
---
guid: GUID-D0A2A7D1-DEA5-4479-8A45-BDDFF4DFE3A8
title: "To Create a Plotter Configuration File for DWFx File Output "
depth: 8
parent_guid: GUID-AD5DF835-6D1B-48E8-B745-0DF6A979B086
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-D0A2A7D1-DEA5-4479-8A45-BDDFF4DFE3A8.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. In the Autodesk Plotter Manager, double-click the Add-a-Plotter Wizard shortcut icon.
3. In the Add-a-Plotter wizard, click Next.
4. On the Add Plotter - Begin page, click My Computer. Click Next.
5. On the Add Plotter - Plotter Model page, select the following values, and click Next:
6. On the Import PCP or PC2 page, click Next.
7. On the Add Plotter - Ports page, select the port to use when plotting. Click Next.
8. On the Add Plotter - Plotter Name page, enter a name to identify the currently configured plotter. Click Next.
9. On the Add Plotter - Finish page, click the Edit Plotter Configuration button to change the default settings for the plotter.
10. After you finish configuring the plotter, click Finish.
11. On the Finish page, click Finish.

guid: GUID-D0BD3D7E-E951-4D14-9DFD-120C1407F9AD
title: "To Detach a PMP File From a PC3 File "
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-E755A113-91B4-42BC-8F65-C7FAA2E02C4E
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-D0BD3D7E-E951-4D14-9DFD-120C1407F9AD.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the plotter configuration from which you want to detach a PMP file.
3. On the Device and Document Settings tab, select User-defined Paper Sizes & Calibration and then select the PMP File Name <>.
4. Click Detach. (If this PC3 file does not have an attached PMP file, the Detach option is unavailable.)
5. Click OK.

guid: GUID-D550C560-FDC0-4A68-A56C-52C98C3DD0A6
title: "About Controlling the Display of User Interface Elements"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-E9708BEF-4C19-49DE-A792-9188A140C27E
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-D550C560-FDC0-4A68-A56C-52C98C3DD0A6.htm
---



---
---
guid: GUID-D55691E6-3D29-4404-99D6-8B7185628EB8
title: "To Add a New Custom Paper Size From Scratch (Nonsystem HDI Drivers Only)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-E755A113-91B4-42BC-8F65-C7FAA2E02C4E
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-D55691E6-3D29-4404-99D6-8B7185628EB8.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the plotter configuration you want to modify.
3. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, click the Device and Document Settings tab.
4. Double-click User-Defined Paper Sizes & Calibration to display the calibration and paper size options. Then select Custom Paper Sizes.
5. Under Custom Paper Sizes, click Add.
6. In the Custom Paper Size Wizard, on the Begin page, select Start from Scratch. Click Next.
7. On the Media Bounds page, in the Units list, select either Inches or Millimeters for paper size.
8. From the Width and Length lists, select the paper width and length. Click Next.
9. On the Printable Area page, in the Top, Bottom, Left, and Right boxes, specify the printable area. Click Next.
10. On the Paper Size Name page, enter a name for the paper size. Click Next.
11. On the File Name page, enter a name for the PMP file.
12. On the Finish page, specify whether the paper source is Sheet-Fed or Roll-Fed. Click Print Test Page to verify the custom size.
13. Click Finish to exit the Custom Paper Size wizard.

---
guid: GUID-D74F3A2B-F506-415F-8F5A-258764C2E26D
title: " arx (AutoLISP)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-D74F3A2B-F506-415F-8F5A-258764C2E26D.htm
---



---
---
guid: GUID-D7905AAC-EEB7-4156-BE0E-0D72CF909FFA
title: "To Add Superscript and Subscript Definitions to a Font"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-13D2F062-4526-4AC5-B447-F982D0A1EA41
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-D7905AAC-EEB7-4156-BE0E-0D72CF909FFA.htm
---

1. Edit your SHP file with an ASCII text editor (for example, Notepad on Windows or TextEdit on Mac OS).
2. Search for the shape definitions of the characters you are replacing. To comment out those definitions so the new definitions can take their place, insert a semicolon in front of each line of the shape definition. The shape definition may continue for a number of lines.
3. Add the first and second values on the second line of the definition, and divide the total by 2 as shown in the following example:

   ```
   *UNIFONT,6,Extended Simplex Roman for UNICODE
   21,7,2,0 21 + 7 = 28, then 28 / 2 = 14. This number is used later.
   ```
4. Add the following lines to the end of the SHP file:

   ```
   *91,8,super_on 
   2,8,(0,14),003,2,1,0 
   *93,8,super_off 
   2,004,2,8,(0,-14),1,0 
   *123,8,sub_on 
   2,8,(0,-14),003,2,1,0 
   *125,8,sub_off 
   2,004,2,8,(0,14),1,0
   ```
5. Save the file.
6. Use the COMPILE command to compile the SHP file.

---

guid: GUID-D91CAC88-0FF3-475E-AF40-6BAF7E182CF4
title: "To Turn Trace Logging On and Off (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-71751025-1ECA-44C5-B7CF-71B728B89AAD
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-D91CAC88-0FF3-475E-AF40-6BAF7E182CF4.htm
---

2. Click File Toggle Trace Log.
3. In the Open Log dialog box, in the File Name box, enter a name for the log file.
4. Browse to the folder you want to save the log file to. Click Save.
5. Click File Toggle Trace Log again to disable logging.

---
guid: GUID-DBC72668-153D-48F4-9C19-87053975A97C
title: " alloc (AutoLISP)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-DBC72668-153D-48F4-9C19-87053975A97C.htm
---



---
---
guid: GUID-DC1713AC-D79F-456B-87E8-1656130CB23B
title: "About Removing Reactors (AutoLISP/ActiveX)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-89966743-6860-42BD-AA34-714E5B28863E
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-DC1713AC-D79F-456B-87E8-1656130CB23B.htm
---

* - Tests to determine if a reactor object is enabled. For example:

  ```
  (vlr-added-p circleReactor)
  T
  ```
* - Disables a reactor. For example:

  ```
  (vlr-remove circleReactor)
  #<VLR-Object-reactor>
  ```
* - Disables all reactors or all reactors of the specified type. For example:

  ```
  (vlr-remove-all)
  ((:VLR-Object-Reactor #<VLR-Object-Reactor>))

  (vlr-remove-all :VLR-DWG-Reactor)
  nil
  ```
* - Enables a disabled reactor object. For example:

  ```
  (vlr-add circleReactor)
  #<VLR-Object-reactor>
  ```

---
---
guid: GUID-DC1B25FE-E063-486C-B90C-565AB5E87BBC
title: "To Create A Personal Information Exchange (PFX) File"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-0A93626D-8389-45FC-969B-B86A2F37D691
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-DC1B25FE-E063-486C-B90C-565AB5E87BBC.htm
---

```
"C:\Program Files (x86)\Windows Kits\10\bin\x64\pvk2pfx.exe" -pvk MyCert.pvk -pi MyPassword -spc MyCert.cer -pfx MyCert.pfx -po MyPassword
```

* - Specifies the location of the
  tool.
* - Specifies the Private Key (PVK) file that should be used to create the PFX file. In this example, the file is named
  .
* - Specifies the password assigned to the PVK file. In this example, the password is MyPassword.
* - Specifies the Certificate (CER) or Software Publisher Certificate (SPC) file that should be used to create the PFX file. In this example, the file is named
  .
* - Specifies the Personal Information Exchange (PFX) file that will be created by the
  tool. In this example, the file is named
  .
* - Specifies the password to be assigned to the PFX file. In this example, the password is MyPassword.

1. Make a private key and digital certificate, or use the PVK and CER existing files that were previously made with the
   tool. See the "To Make a Digital Certificate" topic for a basic understanding of how to use the
   tool.
2. Click the Windows Start button Windows System Command Prompt to display the Windows Command prompt.
3. In the Windows Command Prompt window, type
   and press Enter to set the
   folder as the current working folder. If you are using a different working folder, specify that location instead.
4. Type the location of the
   and the arguments that should be executed.

---
guid: GUID-DDF57ED1-AFD9-4256-B0AF-201D5DC30D87
title: "FAQ: What user license mode is being used by this product?"
depth: 3
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-DDF57ED1-AFD9-4256-B0AF-201D5DC30D87.htm
---

* If \_PKSER doesn't equal "000-00000000", then the user is using a perpetual license.
* If \_PKSER equals "000-00000000" and both ONLINEUSERID and ONLINEUSERNAME don't equal "", then the user is on subscription.

guid: GUID-DE12B4F3-3A24-4121-B417-569050C0A7CA
title: "Using Angles and Setting Up Points"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-D0CF600F-566E-4D79-9DEB-3039A97E5348
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Tutorials/files/GUID-DE12B4F3-3A24-4121-B417-569050C0A7CA.htm

---
---
guid: GUID-DE1BB0EB-3D3F-479B-A42F-B905D64212BD
title: "To Define an Application that Includes a Project File (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-344C2323-DFE0-4248-B100-9FAA1E50FE6B
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-DE1BB0EB-3D3F-479B-A42F-B905D64212BD.htm
---

1. In Visual LISP, click File Make Application New Application Wizard.
2. In the Make Application wizard, on the Wizard Mode page, click Expert. Click Next.
3. On the Application Directory page, Application Location, click Browse and specify a location for the application file and application make file.
4. In the Application Name box, enter a name for the application and application make files. Click Next.
5. On the Application Options page, select the application options you want to use when building the application. Click Next.
6. On the LISP Files to Include page, click the Program Files Type drop-down list and select Visual LISP Project Files. Click Add and specify the project file to add, and then click Open.
7. Add additional files to the application as needed. Click Next.
8. On the Resource Files to Include page, click the Resource Files Type drop-down list and select the type of files you want to add. Click Add and specify the resource file to add, and then click Open.
9. Add additional files to the application as needed. Click Next.
10. On the Application Compilation Options page, select Standard or Optimize and Link. Click Next.
11. On the Review Selections/Build Application page, click Finish.

---

---
guid: GUID-DEAF5553-C4EA-43CD-BADD-038251B8E1CA
title: "To Set a Breakpoint that Interrupts Program Execution (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-9ADDB1E6-4759-476F-808E-B50984EAC019
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-DEAF5553-C4EA-43CD-BADD-038251B8E1CA.htm
---

1. In the Visual LISP text editor window, position the cursor in front of the open parenthesis of the code expression that you want the program to be interrupted on.
2. Click Debug Toggle Breakpoint.
3. Click Tools Load Text in Editor.
4. At the AutoCAD command prompt, enter the command or function to begin the execution of the program.
5. Click Debug Continue to resume execution of the program.

---
---
guid: GUID-DFDAE6CD-E753-4D01-9D9B-4D1F66B1DE6E
title: "About Adding an Entity without Using the Command Function (AutoLISP)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-B150646B-5F8F-460A-A5D6-AF7BD467B638
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-DFDAE6CD-E753-4D01-9D9B-4D1F66B1DE6E.htm
---

```
(entmake '((0 . "CIRCLE") ; Object type
  (8 . "MYLAYER")         ; Layer
  (10 5.0 7.0 0.0)        ; Center point
  (40 . 1.0)              ; Radius
))
```

* The first or second member in the list must specify the entity type. The type must be a valid DXF group code. If the first member does not specify the type, it can specify only the name of the entity: group -1 (the name is not saved in the database).
* AutoCAD must recognize all objects that the entity list refers to. There is one exception:
  accepts new layer names.
* Any internal fields passed to
  are ignored.
* cannot create viewport entities.

```
(entmake '(
  (0 . "MTEXT")
  (100 . "AcDbEntity") ; Required for all post-R12 entities.
  (8 . "ALAYER")
  (100 . "AcDbMText")  ; Identifies the entity as MTEXT.
  (10 4.0 4.0 0.0)
  (1 . "Some\\Ptext")
))
```

guid: GUID-E1BD97BB-FAE6-40DF-B7B3-CE4BBD0241C4
title: "About AutoLISP Documentation (AutoLISP)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-A0E9D801-8BE9-4BF1-85E8-3807E15F3B71
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-E1BD97BB-FAE6-40DF-B7B3-CE4BBD0241C4.htm
---

* documentation describes what every AutoLISP function does and provides basic samples to see how a function can be used.
* documentation contains step-by-step instructions guiding you toward writing a working AutoLISP program.
* documentation assumes you have some experience with AutoCAD. Prior experience with AutoLISP is not required.

* Details on the concepts and structures of the AutoLISP language.
* Provides a summary of all AutoLISP functions by category and information on AutoLISP error codes.
* Describes how to develop and test AutoLISP programs.
* Explains how to design and implement dialog boxes with AutoLISP applications.

title: "Passing Parameters to Functions"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-D0CF600F-566E-4D79-9DEB-3039A97E5348
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Tutorials/files/GUID-E204B037-D6DF-4DDC-9061-E1A2F6E1FA62.htm
---



---
---
guid: GUID-E242568F-F4FE-4567-90C5-89D3F40ECBA6
title: "To Launch and Attach an Instance of AutoCAD to VS Code for Debugging "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-09B4C574-F9FB-4F97-8728-5EAB64E13595
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-E242568F-F4FE-4567-90C5-89D3F40ECBA6.htm
---

1. In Visual Studio Code, open and activate an editor window that contains the AutoLISP source code to debug.
2. On the Activity Bar, click Debug and Run (or click View menu > Debug).
3. Click the Configurations drop-down list and choose one of the following configurations:
   * – Launches a new instance of AutoCAD and attaches VS Code to that instance
   * – Allows you to attach VS Code to an instance of AutoCAD that is already running
4. Click Start Debugging or press F5.
5. If you choose AutoLISP Debug: Attach from the Configurations list, choose acad (or AutoCAD on Mac OS) from the list of running processes.

* – Continues the execution of the AutoLISP program to the next breakpoint
* – An entire expression (and all nested expressions) are evaluated, then execution stops at the end of the overall expression
* – Execution begins and halts before evaluation of the inner parenthetical expression
* – Execution resumes executing the rest of the expressions within a function and then execution halts on the outermost parenthetical expression
* – Terminates and restarts the debugging operation; the AutoLISP source (LSP) file in the active window is automatically reloaded into the AutoCAD application
* – Terminates the debugging operation and disconnects VS Code from the AutoCAD application

---
guid: GUID-E2BCE056-8026-47C4-9CC2-1DF5A9846BAE
title: "To Open a Symbol Service Dialog Box and Update a Symbol (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-540202CA-0929-4CBB-909F-33DE5EBD441F
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-E2BCE056-8026-47C4-9CC2-1DF5A9846BAE.htm
---

1. In the Visual LISP text editor or Console window, highlight the name of any symbol in your program's source code.
2. Click View Symbol Service.
   * A toolbar
   * A Name field, where you can enter or change the symbol to work on
   * A Value field that displays the symbol's value or its initial substring
   * A series of check boxes for symbol flags
3. To update the value of the displayed symbol, enter an expression or value in the Value field.

guid: GUID-E460B577-941D-4CB5-96D1-62A087709DA6
title: "To Insert a Region "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-94E5E163-3425-4B1A-9967-143DFC50842F
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-E460B577-941D-4CB5-96D1-62A087709DA6.htm
---

1. Activate the editor window that contains the AutoLISP expressions you want to place inside a region.
2. Select the expressions you want to place inside a region.
3. Right-click and choose Insert Region.
4. Optionally, add a meaningful description after the
   comment to identify the code within the region.

guid: GUID-E69C877D-F84B-4282-807D-E084C931D533
title: "About Custom and Third-party Application Compatibility"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-D54B0935-1638-4F97-8B37-1EC3635A1E71
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-E69C877D-F84B-4282-807D-E084C931D533.htm
---

* – Custom images stored in BMP files that use the color value 192,192,192 for transparency must be updated to PNG files with a transparent color. If the images are not updated, the pixels assigned the color value 192,192,192 will be displayed as that color instead of being transparent.
* – No changes should be needed, but verify that no deprecated commands and system variables are being used.
* – Programs that use the
  function might need to be updated, and verify that no deprecated commands and system variables are being used.
* – Programs that assign a password to a drawing must be modified and any program that uses the
  method should be reviewed to see if the
  method should be changed to use the
  method that was introduced with AutoCAD 2015-based products. Programs developed for AutoCAD 2014-based products and earlier should also be reviewed and updated for proper 64-bit compatibility. Statements that reference the
  and
  objects need to be commented out or removed.
* – Programs that assign a password to a drawing, utilize render presets, or statements that reference the
  and
  objects need to be modified or removed. Programs developed for AutoCAD 2018-based products and earlier need to be recompiled to reference the necessary .NET Framework.
* – Programs that assign a password to a drawing, utilize render presets, or statements that reference the
  and
  objects need to be modified or removed. Programs developed for AutoCAD 2018-based products and earlier must reference the files of the latest SDK and be recompiled.
* – No changes should be needed.

---
guid: GUID-E7282714-87B7-4382-93B6-94A92B121AEA
title: "To Add or Edit Code Snippet Definitions "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-94E5E163-3425-4B1A-9967-143DFC50842F
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-E7282714-87B7-4382-93B6-94A92B121AEA.htm
---

* – A unique name for the code snippet; used if no description is provided
* – Defines the name to be typed and displayed in the IntelliSense list to insert the code snippet
* – Expressions that define the code snippet, can contain new lines, tabs, and placeholders
* – Defines the text that should be displayed in the IntelliSense tooltip for the code snippet

```
"ifprogn": 
  {
    "prefix": "ifp",
    "body":
      [
        "(if (${1:testexpr})",
            "\t(progn",
            "\t\t(${2:thenexpr})",
            "\t)",
        ")"
      ],
    "description": "if progn expression"
  }
```

1. In Visual Studio Code or another text editor, open the
   file.
   * –
   * –
2. In the
   file, add your new code snippet or change an existing one.
3. Save the
   file and test the code snippet changes.

guid: GUID-E755A113-91B4-42BC-8F65-C7FAA2E02C4E
title: "About Calibrating Plotters and Setting With Custom Paper Sizes"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-E755A113-91B4-42BC-8F65-C7FAA2E02C4E.htm
---



---
---
guid: GUID-E7883389-689B-43FA-B733-E4179042E6E6
title: "To Adjust Media Settings"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-6B38619A-4ED5-4713-A163-0D3E0A3847B0
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-E7883389-689B-43FA-B733-E4179042E6E6.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the plotter configuration (PC3) file whose media settings you want to change.
3. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, click the Device and Document Settings tab.
4. Double-click Media to view the media settings.
5. Do one of the following:
   * Under Media Source and Size, select a paper source from the Source list. If appropriate, select a roll width from the Width list or a tray from the Tray Type list. Under Size, select the paper size you want to use. Select Automatic to tell the printer to select the appropriate paper source.
   * Under Media Type, select one of the available media types.
   * Under Print on Both Sides (Duplex Printing), select Short Side or Long Side. This setting may not be available for your plotter.
   * Under Media Destination, specify one of the available options, for example, cutting. This setting may not be available for your plotter.
6. Click OK.

---
guid: GUID-E7EC9E8A-D8B2-4205-BD3B-15763EC4F94C
title: "To Complete a Word by Matching in the Console Window (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 7
parent_guid: GUID-F605EFDD-2B63-4092-9BC2-BEEDD413DCAE
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-E7EC9E8A-D8B2-4205-BD3B-15763EC4F94C.htm
---

1. In Visual LISP, at the Console window prompt, type the text in a line of code you want to match.
2. Press Ctrl+Spacebar to invoke Complete Word by Match. Visual LISP finds the last word you entered that begins with the letters you entered.
3. Press Ctrl+Spacebar until the line of code you are looking for is located.

   .

   extension can be selected.

5. Click Apply.

---
guid: GUID-E8328DF6-43FF-47AA-8524-72B962A9D552
title: "About Wild-Card Matching (AutoLISP)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-5F53273B-F301-4EA3-ABBC-524FA961E4F6
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-E8328DF6-43FF-47AA-8524-72B962A9D552.htm
---

* Alphabetic characters and numerals are treated literally in the pattern.
* Brackets can be used to specify optional characters or a range of letters or digits.
* A question mark () matches a single character.
* An asterisk () matches a sequence of characters; and, certain other special characters have special meanings within the pattern. When you use the character at the beginning and end of the search pattern, you can locate the desired portion anywhere in the string.

```

"this is a string - test1 test2 the end"
```

```

T
```

```

nil
```

```

T
```

```

T
```

---
---
guid: GUID-EBCB6710-0290-44CB-94B3-6C1064E82BB4
title: "About Initializing Modes and Values (DCL)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-C29336BC-4849-4149-9CA4-EC0D740D7CD6
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-EBCB6710-0290-44CB-94B3-6C1064E82BB4.htm
---

* Making it the initial keyboard focus of the dialog box
* Disabling or enabling it
* Highlighting its contents, if it is an edit box or image

```
(setq name_str "Kenobi")       ; Default.
(set_tile "lastname" name_str) ; Initializes field.
(mode_tile "lastname" 2)       ; 2 sets focus to tile.
```

```
(mode_tile "lastname" 3)       ; 3 selects box contents.
```

---
---
guid: GUID-EBE15E06-23FB-4A8F-B4CA-48B53E789FB7
title: "To Modify a Standard Paper Size"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-E755A113-91B4-42BC-8F65-C7FAA2E02C4E
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-EBE15E06-23FB-4A8F-B4CA-48B53E789FB7.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the plotter configuration you want to modify.
3. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, click the Device and Document Settings tab.
4. Double-click User-Defined Paper Sizes & Calibration to display the calibration and paper size settings.
5. Select Modify Standard Paper Sizes.
6. Under Modify Standard Paper Sizes, select the paper size you want to adjust. Then click Modify.
7. In the Custom Paper Size wizard, adjust the printable area as necessary. Then click Finish to exit the Custom Paper Size wizard.

---

* - Opens a file for access by the AutoLISP I/O functions.
* - Writes a string to the screen or to an open file.
* - Writes one character to the screen or to an open file.
* - Reads a string from the keyboard or from an open file, until an end-of-line marker is encountered.
* - Returns the decimal ASCII code representing the character read from the keyboard input buffer or from an open file.
* – Prints an expression to the command line or writes an expression to an open file.
* – Prints an expression to the command line or writes an expression to an open file.
* – Closes a file opened with the function.

guid: GUID-EF2D73CE-9B75-4532-AF2F-DD6F0C36C3FD
title: "About Passing Pick Points to AutoCAD Commands (AutoLISP)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-75F19C76-78D0-443B-BC39-EB9FEB4650B1
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-EF2D73CE-9B75-4532-AF2F-DD6F0C36C3FD.htm
---

```
    ;Draws a circle
 ;Draws a line
               ;Gets the last entity 
                                  ;  added to the drawing
                  ;Sets the trim point
    ;Performs the trim
```

1. Draws a circle centered at (5,5) with a radius of 2.
2. Draws a line from (3,5) to (7,5).
3. Creates a variable that is the name of the last object added to the database.
4. Creates a variable that is a point on the circle. (This point selects the portion of the circle to be trimmed.)
5. Performs the TRIM command by selecting the object (the line) and by selecting the point specified by .

guid: GUID-EF8C5586-BA1F-4EA6-BAD1-6BA792B601F0
title: "About Obtaining Entity Information (AutoLISP)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-B150646B-5F8F-460A-A5D6-AF7BD467B638
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-EF8C5586-BA1F-4EA6-BAD1-6BA792B601F0.htm
---

* Layer is 0
* Linetype is CONTINUOUS
* Elevation is 0

```
(defun C:PRINTDXF ( )
  (setq ent (entlast))               ; Set ent to last entity.
  (setq entl (entget ent))           ; Set entl to association list of last entity.
  (setq ct 0)                        ; Set ct (a counter) to 0.
  (textpage)                         ; Switch to the text screen.
  (princ "\nentget of last entity:")
  (repeat (length entl)              ; Repeat for number of members in list:
    (print (nth ct entl))            ; Output a newline, then each list member.
    (setq ct (1+ ct))                ; Increments the counter by one.
  )
 (princ)                             ; Exit quietly.
)
```

```
entget of last entity:
(-1 . <Entity name: 1bbd1c8>)
(0 . "LINE")
(330 . <Entity name: 1bbd0c8>)
(5 . "69")
(100 . "AcDbEntity")
(67 . 0)
(410 . "Model")
(8 . "0")
(100 . "AcDbLine")
(10 1.0 2.0 0.0)
(11 6.0 6.0 0.0)
(210 0.0 0.0 1.0)
```

```
(cdr (assoc 0 entl))
```

parent_guid: GUID-C29336BC-4849-4149-9CA4-EC0D740D7CD6
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-F208561B-5C2E-47FE-BD24-520DF75DE92A.htm
---

```
(action_tile
  "myslider"
  "(slider_action $value $reason)"
)

(action_tile
  "slider_info"
  "(ebox_action $value $reason)"
)

.
.
.

(defun slider_action(val why)
  (if (or (= why 2) (= why 1))   ; Check reason code.
    (set_tile "slider_info" val) ; Show interim result.
  )
)

(defun ebox_action(val why)
  (if (or (= why 2) (= why 1))   ; Check reason code.
    (set_tile "myslider" val)    ; Show interim result.
  )
)
```

---
guid: GUID-F25D028C-061C-4884-9D0D-314FC728BB01
title: "When I Click Debug, Why doesn’t the Debug Operation Start or it Starts but Fails? "
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-F25D028C-061C-4884-9D0D-314FC728BB01.htm
---

* file might not have been created or configured correctly
* file is placed in a workspace and not a folder
* Make sure the file you are trying to debug is of the LSP or MNL type; if you created a new file, make sure you save it with the appropriate file extension
* Make sure the LISPSYS system variable is set to 1 or 2, if you are running AutoCAD on Windows

* attribute of
  + Doesn’t contain or contains an incorrect path to the AutoCAD executable, see
  + Path isn’t specified as an absolute path to the AutoCAD executable
  + On Mac OS,
    is being used as a path separator instead of the expected
* attribute of
  + Doesn’t contain or contains the incorrect or case-sensitive name of the AutoCAD process

guid: GUID-F3168985-3DA2-475F-AD0E-31FF112BE13B
title: "To Run a Compiled Program from the Visual LISP Console Window (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-597C2B69-7389-4BF7-B780-25B7D77FCFA0
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-F3168985-3DA2-475F-AD0E-31FF112BE13B.htm
---

1. At the Visual LISP Console window, enter an AutoLISP statement that uses the load function.

   ```
   (load "c:/program files/Autodesk/<AutoCAD installation directory>/sample/visuallisp/yinyang.fas")
   ```
2. At the Visual LISP Console window prompt, enter the name of the function you want to run, enclosing the name in parentheses.

   ```
   (yinyang)
   ```

---
guid: GUID-F3333A6A-DE51-4864-BEA6-1C6C5BF9BEF8
title: "To Create a Hatch Pattern with Multiple Lines "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-79B99823-7600-4CAB-BD12-04D5103D90CB
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-F3333A6A-DE51-4864-BEA6-1C6C5BF9BEF8.htm
---

1. Open an existing PAT file or create a new file in a text editor that saves in ASCII format (for example, Notepad on Windows or TextEdit on Mac OS).
2. Create a header line that begins with an asterisk and includes a pattern name that is no more than 31 characters in length.
3. Optionally, include a description for the hatch pattern by adding a comma and descriptive text after the pattern name.
4. Create a descriptor line that includes
   * An angle at which the line is drawn
   * An
     origin point
   * A
     of any value if you want to offset alternating lines in the line family
   * A
     of any value
   * A value for a dash length
   * A value for a dot length
   * An optional second value for a different dash length
   * An optional second value for a different dot length
5. Create a second line including all the parameters in the previous step.
6. Optionally, create additional lines to complete the multiple-line hatch pattern.
7. Add a blank line after the last descriptor line.

---

title: "To Delete a Custom Paper Size"

guid: GUID-F41FB58A-4645-404E-98B7-D4978A9A790B
title: " vlax-curve-getPointAtDist (AutoLISP/ActiveX)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-F41FB58A-4645-404E-98B7-D4978A9A790B.htm

---
guid: GUID-F46266B6-C440-496F-882D-0B0F3B6EE7DB
title: "To Specify or Modify Settings for Plotted DWFx Files"
depth: 8
parent_guid: GUID-AD5DF835-6D1B-48E8-B745-0DF6A979B086
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-F46266B6-C440-496F-882D-0B0F3B6EE7DB.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print.
2. In the Plot dialog box, under Printer/Plotter, in the Name list, select the DWFx plotter configuration file you want to edit. Click Properties.
3. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, Device and Document Settings tab, select Custom Properties in the tree window.
4. In the Access Custom Dialog group, click the Custom Properties button.
5. In the DWFx ePlot Properties dialog box, select the options you want. Click OK.
6. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, click OK.
7. In the Changes to a Printer Configuration dialog box, do one of the following:
   * Select Apply Changes for the Current Plot Only — to specify a one-time override of the configuration settings that is not saved to the ePlot configuration file.
   * Select Save Changes to the Following File — to save the configuration changes to the current DWFx configuration file.
8. Click OK twice.
9. In the Browse for Plot File dialog box, navigate to the folder location you want to save. Click Save.
10. Click OK.

guid: GUID-F469D307-86E6-4081-A33B-CD9AD94A4C20
title: "About -TEXT and TEXTEVAL in AutoLISP"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-16DC15FC-5329-492E-B66A-401D49CF971F
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-F469D307-86E6-4081-A33B-CD9AD94A4C20.htm
---



---
---
guid: GUID-F4A63A70-EB72-4F7D-A90C-3C5ABD6864A9
title: "About Designing Dialog Boxes (DCL)"
depth: 3
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-F4A63A70-EB72-4F7D-A90C-3C5ABD6864A9.htm
---

* A dialog box should never appear to be cluttered, it makes for an ineffective and hard to use design. Take advantage of white space to spread controls out from each other.
* Individuals often scan a dialog box from upper-left to lower-right, so placing the most commonly used tiles in these areas makes for a more effective design.
* Arrange sections of the dialog box logically into rows or columns so users can scan them from left to right or from top to bottom.
* Align related entry fields (such as edit boxes or list boxes) both vertically and horizontally, so that when users switch fields by pressing Tab, the cursor moves in a straight, orthogonal line.
* If there is a natural order for entering data—such as the
  ,
  , and
  of coordinates—order the fields in the same way. Align boxed areas both vertically and horizontally. Do not leave a lot of white space around or between boxed areas. Extend their width to the right, if necessary.
* Nesting dialog boxes can be helpful in hiding less commonly used options from the user, but avoid going too many nesting levels deep. When a nested dialog box is called, the user should return to the calling dialog box.
* The dialog boxes of an application should be internally consistent, and consistent with related applications. A familiar dialog box is easier to understand if its design is consistent with other dialog boxes in the application, related applications, or the host system.
* Use standard definitions for dialog box controls. This reduces your work, contributes to consistency, and makes it easier for users to learn and use your dialog boxes.
* Provide reasonable defaults for all entries and options. Well-chosen defaults can help users complete a dialog box quickly and easily. It is recommended that you update the default values—in other words, that you save the user's previous settings and use them as the new defaults—each time the dialog box is used.
* You should provide a Help facility. It is recommended that the main dialog box of your application have a Help button that displays a basic topic file that describes how to use the options of the dialog box. In most cases, the Help button should call the Help facility using the
  function.

guid: GUID-F605EFDD-2B63-4092-9BC2-BEEDD413DCAE
title: "About Completing a Word by Matching (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-74E1A334-E516-478D-B33D-3BC55E1176DD
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-F605EFDD-2B63-4092-9BC2-BEEDD413DCAE.htm
---

```
(setq origin (getpoint "\nOrigin of inyn sign: "))
(setq radius (getdist "\nRadius of inyn sign: " origin))
(setq half-r (/ radius 2))
(setq origin-x (car origin))
(command "._circle" origin radius)
```

(vlax-method-applicable-p WhatsMyLine "Copy")

guid: GUID-F7389E0F-BD5E-4A7C-9C58-AF47E1A23EF8
title: "To Open an AutoLISP or DCL File "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-8BCC1A08-B530-4220-A199-4CB40FCB20ED
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-F7389E0F-BD5E-4A7C-9C58-AF47E1A23EF8.htm

---
---
guid: GUID-F75A21AC-E803-44E8-8F35-BBF1201D772A
title: "To Preview a Dialog Box (Visual LISP IDE/DCL)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-98B06029-E62D-4644-9E68-1964907C9147
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-F75A21AC-E803-44E8-8F35-BBF1201D772A.htm
---

1. In the Visual LISP Editor, click File Open File.
2. In the Open File to Edit/View dialog box, in the Files of Type drop-down list, select DCL Source Files. Browse to and select the DCL file you want to preview. Click Open.
3. Click Tools Interface Tools Preview DCL in Editor to display a list of all the dialog boxes defined in the current text editor window.
4. In the Enter the Dialog Name dialog box, select the dialog box name from the drop-down list that you want to preview and click OK.
5. Click the OK or Cancel button to complete previewing the dialog box.

title: "To Configure a Plotter Driver for Raster File Output "
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-AFA15B89-A755-4FC1-9A13-E0F6357AE6BD
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-F7D6A22D-CD86-477A-9365-67F5B727E85E.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the Add-a-Plotter Wizard shortcut icon.
3. On the Begin page, select My Computer. Click Next.
4. On the Plotter Model page under Manufacturers, select Raster File Formats. Under Model, select the type of raster file that you want to create. Click Next.
5. On the Import PCP or PC2 page, click Next to continue.
6. On the Ports page, select Plot to File. Click Next.
7. On the Plotter Name page, enter a name for the plotter configuration file. Click Next.
8. On the Finish page, click Finish.

---
---
guid: GUID-F8074AA9-F361-4960-B628-681465B74229
title: "About Lists (AutoLISP)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-7E568541-F1D0-49C4-B878-15880486825F
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-F8074AA9-F361-4960-B628-681465B74229.htm
---

* - Creates a new list with any number of values.
* - Appends values to an existing list, and returns a new list.
* - Adds an element to the beginning of a list, or constructs a dotted list.
* - Returns an integer indicating the number of elements in a list.
* - Searches an association list for an element and returns that association list entry.
* - Returns the first element of a list.
* - Returns a list containing all but the first element of the specified list.
* - Returns the nth element of a list.
* - Searches a list for an old item and returns a copy of the list with a new item substituted in place of every occurrence of the old item.

---
guid: GUID-F8C573FB-F479-441B-9DEE-14EB19268E43
title: "To Configure a Network, Nonsystem Plotter"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-D1786BA2-1CB1-4585-AA6A-6ED8088D4B28
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-F8C573FB-F479-441B-9DEE-14EB19268E43.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the Add-a-Plotter Wizard shortcut icon.
3. In the Add-a-Plotter wizard, read the Introduction, and then click Next to advance to the Add Plotter - Begin page.
4. On the Add Plotter - Begin page, click Network Plotter Server. Click Next.
5. On the Add Plotter - Network Plotter page, enter the share name of the network plotter server that you want to use.
6. On the Add Plotter - Plotter Model page, select a manufacturer and model. Click Next.
7. On the Import PCP or PC2 page, click Next to continue.
8. On the Add Plotter - Plotter Name page, enter a name to identify the currently configured plotter. Click Next.
9. When you reach the Add Plotter - Finish page, you can click Finish to exit the Add-a-Plotter wizard.

---
guid: GUID-FA5F2E08-24F5-4947-A470-6CA84E404F2A
title: "About Xrecord Objects (AutoLISP)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-9AED35A1-5CB2-43D8-88ED-CBE95E54798D
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-FA5F2E08-24F5-4947-A470-6CA84E404F2A.htm
---

```
(defun C:MAKEXRECORD( / xrec xname )
  ; create the xrecord's data list.
  (setq xrec '((0 . "XRECORD")(100 . "AcDbXrecord")
    (1 . "This is a test xrecord list")
    (10 1.0 2.0 0.0) (40 . 3.14159) (50 . 3.14159)
    (62 . 1) (70 . 180))
  )

  ; use entmakex to create the xrecord with no owner.
  (setq xname (entmakex xrec))

  ; add the new xrecord to the named object dictionary.
  (dictadd (namedobjdict) "XRECLIST" xname)
 (princ)
)

(defun C:LISTXRECORD ( / xlist )
  ; find the xrecord in the named object dictionary.
  (setq xlist (dictsearch (namedobjdict) "XRECLIST"))

  ; print out the xrecord's data list.
  (princ xlist)
 (princ)
)
```

```
((-1 . <Entity name: 7ffffb05ee0>) (0 . XRECORD) (5 . 1E6) (102 . {ACAD_REACTORS) (330 . <Entity name: 7ffffb038c0>) (102 . }) (330 . <Entity name: 7ffffb038c0>) (100 . AcDbXrecord) (280 . 1) (1 . This is a test xrecord list) (10 1.0 2.0 0.0) (40 . 3.14159) (50 . 3.14159) (62 . 1) (70 . 180))
```

---
---
guid: GUID-FA8BBFB8-5C3E-4742-A3A2-CBCDB168FB08
title: "About Attaching Extended Data to an Entity (AutoLISP)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-A94BC605-5517-437F-A6FE-D3EB8116A01A
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-FA8BBFB8-5C3E-4742-A3A2-CBCDB168FB08.htm
---

```
; Gets the association list of definition data
; for the last entity.
(setq lastent (entget (entlast)))

; Registers the application name.
(regapp "NEWDATA")

(setq exdata                        ; Sets the variable
  '((-3 ("NEWDATA"                  ; exdata equal to the
    (1000 . "This is a new thing!") ; new extended data—
  )))                               ; in this case, a text
)                                   ; string.

; Appends new data list to entity's list.
(setq newent
  (append lastent exdata)) 

; Modifies the entity with the new definition data.
(entmod newent)
```

```
(entget (car (entsel)) '("NEWDATA"))
```

title: "About Raster Image Compression (PostScript)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-76F485FF-0C3E-4EE1-A602-66A09D94C706

---
guid: GUID-FB3BA875-6508-4ADB-BEA3-80A1C9D451FF
title: "To Set Up a Microsoft Visual FoxPro Data Source Using ODBC"
depth: 4
parent_guid: GUID-1C006BB3-9909-420B-B5D7-791E2B104C46
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-FB3BA875-6508-4ADB-BEA3-80A1C9D451FF.htm
---

1. Click the Windows Start button Windows System Control Panel.
2. Double-click the Administrative Tools icon, and then double-click Data Sources (ODBC).
3. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, do one of the following:
   * Click the User DSN tab to create a data source that is visible only to you and can be used only on the computer you create it in.
   * Click the System DSN tab to create a data source that is visible to all users who have access rights to the computer.
   * Click the File DSN tab to create a data source that can be shared with other users who have the same ODBC drivers installed on their systems.
4. Click Add.
5. Select the Microsoft Visual FoxPro Driver, and then click Finish.
6. Enter a name for your data source in Data Source Name, and select a type in Database Type.
7. Click Browse, and then locate and select the database you want to configure. Click Open.
8. In the ODBC Visual FoxPro Setup dialog box, click OK.
9. In the ODBC Data Source Administrator dialog box, click OK.

---

guid: GUID-FB3EC778-96B9-4EB4-AB36-FB427E74D263
title: " vlr-reactions (AutoLISP/ActiveX)"
depth: 4
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP-Reference/files/GUID-FB3EC778-96B9-4EB4-AB36-FB427E74D263.htm

---
---
guid: GUID-FB699DA4-1DF3-49DC-8CED-88E30D92DD81
title: "To Adjust Serial Port Settings"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-863C7A61-8F01-4E53-972A-B553AB8D7793
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-FB699DA4-1DF3-49DC-8CED-88E30D92DD81.htm
---

1. Click Application menu Print Manage Plotters.
2. Double-click the plotter configuration (PC3) file whose serial port settings you want to change.
3. In the Plotter Configuration Editor, click the Ports tab.
4. Click Show All Ports and select Plot to the Following Port.
5. Select the serial port that you want to use and click Configure Port.
6. In the Settings for COM Port dialog box, select a baud rate and protocol for your device.
7. Select a Flow Control method.
   * Enables Clear to Send handshaking. This monitors pin 5 of a 25-pin serial port or pin 8 of a 9-pin serial port. CTS is an input bit, monitored for an output from the plotter or printer.
   * Enables Data Set Ready handshaking. This monitors pin 6 of a 25-pin serial port, or pin 6 of a 9-pin serial port. DSR is an input bit, monitored for an output from the printer or plotter.
   * Enables Received Line Signal Detector handshaking. This is sometimes called Data Carrier Detect or DCD. It's an input pin that can be monitored for an output from the plotter. It's on pin 8 of a 25-pin serial port and on pin 1 of a 9-pin serial port.
   * Controls the Request to Send output bit. This sends a signal to the printer or plotter on pin 4 of a 25-pin serial port or on pin 7 of a 9-pin serial port.
   * Controls the Data Terminal Ready output pin. This sends a signal to the printer or plotter on pin 20 of a 25-pin serial port or on pin 4 of a 9-pin serial port.
8. Click OK to close the Advanced Settings for COM Port dialog box.
9. Click OK to close the Settings for COM Port dialog box.
10. Click OK.

---

---
guid: GUID-FCA90242-7748-482B-BA16-E70C7511F468
title: "To Change the Display Properties of a Palette"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-CF105B57-A6CB-48B2-B129-6E73C4B74D11
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-Customization/files/GUID-FCA90242-7748-482B-BA16-E70C7511F468.htm
---

1. Click
   .
2. In the Customize tab, Customizations In
   pane, expand Workspaces, and select the workspace containing the palette that you want to modify.
3. In the Workspace Contents pane, click the plus sign (+) next to Palettes to expand it.
4. Select the palette that you want to modify.
5. In the Properties pane, do any or all of the following:
   * In the Show box, select an option (No, Yes, or Do Not Change).
   * In the Orientation box, select an option (Floating, Top, Bottom, Left, or Right).
   * In the Allow Docking box, select an option (No, Yes, or Do Not Change).
   * In the Auto Hide box, select an option (On, Off, or Do Not Change).
   * In the Use Transparency box, select an option (No, Yes, or Do Not Change).
   * In the Transparency Amount box, enter a number (if applicable).
   * In the Default Group box, select a tool palette group (Tool Palettes window only).
   * In the Height box, enter a number. A value of 0 is equivalent to Do Not Change.
   * In the Width box, enter a number. A value of 0 is equivalent to Do Not Change.
6. Click Apply.

guid: GUID-FD9081C8-0ADA-459F-924E-555642D1A39A
title: "Formatting AutoLISP Files "
depth: 3
parent_guid: nan
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-FD9081C8-0ADA-459F-924E-555642D1A39A.htm

---
guid: GUID-FDB99D24-AED4-46E6-865A-96DA7B784065
title: "To Enable and Set the Form-closing Comment Style (Visual LISP IDE)"
depth: 7
parent_guid: GUID-C4D0DA99-F11B-4DAD-A709-69175EDC5E14
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-FDB99D24-AED4-46E6-865A-96DA7B784065.htm
---

1. In the Visual LISP IDE, click Tools Environment Options Visual LISP Format Options.
2. In the Format Options dialog box, Closing Parenthesis Style, select Close At the New Line with Inner Indentation or Close At the New Line with Outer Indentation.
3. In the Form-closing Comment Prefix box, enter a new value. Click OK.

---
guid: GUID-FE43302E-AC21-4C0B-B61B-A10751A9E263
title: "To View the Properties of a VLA-Object (AutoLISP/ActiveX)"
depth: 6
parent_guid: GUID-61113D8A-EDFB-4A9B-8CA7-CFFDB0D80C63
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-FE43302E-AC21-4C0B-B61B-A10751A9E263.htm
---

1. Store an object in a variable using
   .
2. Do one of the following:
3. * At the AutoCAD Command prompt, enter
     .

     ```

     ; IAcadApplication: An instance of the AutoCAD application
     ; Property values:
     ;   ActiveDocument = #<VLA-OBJECT IAcadDocument 000002569b4802d8>
     ;   Application (RO) = #<VLA-OBJECT IAcadApplication 00007ff78ec15be0>
     ;   Caption (RO) = "Autodesk AutoCAD 2025 - [Drawing1.dwg]"
     ;   Documents (RO) = #<VLA-OBJECT IAcadDocuments 00000256aab93c70>
     ;   FullName (RO) = "C:\\Program Files\\Autodesk\\AutoCAD 2025\\acad.exe"
     ;   Height = 1040
     ;   HWND (RO) = 595288
     ;   LocaleId (RO) = 1033
     ;   MenuBar (RO) = #<VLA-OBJECT IAcadMenuBar 00000256aab94248>
     ;   MenuGroups (RO) = #<VLA-OBJECT IAcadMenuGroups 00000256fcb1fea8>
     ;   Name (RO) = "AutoCAD"
     ;   Path (RO) = "C:\\Program Files\\Autodesk\\AutoCAD 2025"
     ;   Preferences (RO) = #<VLA-OBJECT IAcadPreferences 00000256aac5b2e8>
     ;   Initializing VBA System...StatusId (RO) = ...Indexed contents not shown...
     ;   VBE (RO) = #<VLA-OBJECT VBE 00000256ce7ac5f8>
     ;   Version (RO) = "25.0s (LMS Tech)"
     ;   Visible = -1
     ;   Width = 1916
     ;   WindowLeft = 2
     ;   WindowState = 1
     ;   WindowTop = 0
     T
     ```
   * 1. In Visual LISP, click View Inspect.
     2. In the Inspect dialog box, Symbol box, enter the name of the variable you stored the object in. Click OK.

---
guid: GUID-FF4F04CC-9DEF-41C7-8C8A-20635DE22A41
title: "About Safearrays with Variants (AutoLISP/ActiveX)"
depth: 5
parent_guid: GUID-697D55E3-BEED-41BF-A974-E65614B912AE
url: https://help.autodesk.com/cloudhelp/2026/ENU/AutoCAD-AutoLISP/files/GUID-FF4F04CC-9DEF-41C7-8C8A-20635DE22A41.htm
---

```
(setq circCenter (vlax-3d-point '(3.0 3.0 0.0)))
#<variant 8197 ...>
```

```
(setq circCenter (vlax-3d-point 3.0 3.0))
#<variant 8197 ...>
```

```
(vlax-safearray->list (vlax-variant-value circcenter))
(3.0 3.0 0.0)
```

```
(vlax-tmatrix '((1 1 1 0) (1 2 3 0) (2 3 4 5) (2 9 8 3)))
#<variant 8197 ...>
```
